### Alabama Emergency Rental Assistance: 2025 Application Guide
Though we’re a few years removed from the COVID-19 pandemic, its lasting effects are still impacting Alabama families. Many in the state are still struggling to get back on their feet, especially when it comes to meeting their rent obligations. Because lawmakers recognize the critical need, several organizations have created Emergency Rental Assistance Programs (ERAPs).&nbsp;These Alabama-centered programs help support residents who struggle to make ends meet. Emergency rental assistance in Alabama is complicated, so it's best to get familiar with your options if you find yourself in need.Understanding Emergency Rental Assistance in AlabamaEmergency Rental Assistance Programs aim to offer financial aid to renters who have run into financial setbacks. These include job loss, income reduction, and emergencies that interfere with covering housing costs. ERAP programs prevent evictions and relieve Alabama residents of the financial burdens they're struggling with.Several programs and organizations exist to help Alabama residents with rental assistance. If you're looking for help, consider reaching out to one of these program offices.Emergency Rental Assistance (ERA) AlabamaThe Emergency Rental Assistance (ERA) Alabama program provides financial relief to renters facing hardship. The Alabama Housing Finance Authority (AHFA) administers this aid to residents struggling with housing-related expenses. Through ERA Alabama, renters who meet the qualification criteria (including housing instability or a possible eviction ahead) can receive the support they need to remain housed.Alabama emergency rental assistance can differ from place to place, as some areas have their own dedicated programs. These include the city of Birmingham, Tuscaloosa County, Mobile County, and Baldwin County.&nbsp;Emergency Rental Assistance Program (ERAP)Jefferson County offers its residents access to ERAP, the Emergency Rental Assistance Program in the area. Like other emergency rental assistance in Alabama, this program is overseen by the AHFA. It's designed to help renters manage the economic struggles that have arisen, including the impact of the COVID-19 pandemic.&nbsp;ERAP provides financial aid to eligible individuals and households to cover rent arrears, rent payments, and even utility costs. The program works with landlords and tenants alike to ensure that stable housing remains a reality for vulnerable people.Emergency Solutions GrantThe Emergency Solutions Grant (ESG) program isn't limited to Alabama, but it's available in the state. This federal program supports individuals and families who are either homeless or at risk of becoming homeless. In Alabama, ESG funds go to local governments and various nonprofits so that they can provide emergency services. Such services include emergency shelter, rehousing assistance, financial services, and other supportive aid. ESG programs aim to address immediate housing needs so that Alabama residents can have stable housing.Emergency Housing Vouchers (EHV)HUD and Section 8 also offer Emergency Housing Vouchers for qualifying situations. These federal rental assistance vouchers are provided by local public housing agencies. They aim to assist both individuals and families who live in unstable housing situations. In Alabama, EHVs offer rental subsidies to households in need, which enables them to secure affordable housing.&nbsp;Community Action Agencies (CAA)Several Community Action Agencies (CAAs) extend Alabama's efforts to provide low-income families with stable homes. These organizations (usually nonprofits) operate across the state and offer a range of helpful services. Services may include emergency rental assistance, utility assistance, and housing counseling.&nbsp;CAAs work with government agencies and other charitable organizations to combat poverty, and homelessness by extension. Many of these organizations play an important role in ensuring that Alabama residents can afford rent.Some local organizations include the Community Action Association Alabama and the Community Action Agency of Northeast Alabama.Applying for Emergency Rental AssistanceIf you're interested in applying for emergency rental assistance in Alabama, there are a few steps you should take. Research and identify the programs designed to address your needs. Then, review the eligibility requirements to make sure your family qualifies for the program's benefits. From there, you'll need to complete the emergency rental assistance Alabama application form.&nbsp;Proceed slowly to ensure you don't forget any points or sections. Be sure to provide any supporting documents and maintain regular communication with your caseworker. The application and approval process may include some back-and-forth, so stay on top of any updates for quicker processing.If you're struggling to find the right program, visit your local AHFA office, or a nearby Department of Human Resources. A caseworker should be able to help point you in the right direction or make recommendations that apply to your situation.Look for Emergency Rental Assistance in AlabamaPrograms offering emergency rental assistance in Alabama can be helpful for families facing housing insecurity. By being aware of your options, you can pursue the assistance you need to maintain stable housing and overcome hardships.&nbsp;For more on emergency rental assistance, explore the resources available on the Affordable Housing Hub. Take a look at open waiting lists, assistance programs, and much more.

### Alaska Emergency Rental Assistance: 2025 Application Guide
Alaska is home to a population of over 700,000 people who deal with extreme weather conditions. With this relatively low population, Alaska has one of the highest homeless rates in the country at 31.7 out of every 10K people, a 10.43% poverty level, and a 6.9% unemployment rate. To provide solutions, many programs offer help with emergency rental assistance in Alaska.Rental Assistance Programs in AlaskaNumerous options exist for emergency assistance from the Alaska Housing Finance Corporation and the Association of Alaska Housing Authorities. These programs are available to homeless, veterans, elderly, and low-income individuals and families to provide safe, clean, and affordable housing.&nbsp;Senior and Accessible HousingThe program offers one-bedroom apartments with access to an elevator. Some of the requirements for the program include:Residents must be 62 or older.Disabled with income 80% or less of the area median income.You should follow the instructions carefully when filling out the application.New Start VoucherThis rental assistance program is for Alaskan residents nearing the end of their stabilization and Recovery Program. It is a referral-based program where residents who make 50% or less of the median income can apply.Veteran Affairs Supportive Housing ProgramVeterans and their families deserve to live in safe, stable housing. This emergency rental assistance program in Alaska helps homeless veterans and their families pay a portion of their rent. When it comes to applying for the program, residents must meet the following requirements:Must have an income of 50% or less of the median area income.Apply at any Alaska Housing location.Referred by Alaska VA Healthcare System to Alaska HousingFor immediate assistance, contact the Veterans Crisis Hotline.Empowering Choice Housing ProgramSuppose you earn 50% or less of the area median income and are a victim of domestic violence, sexual assault, etc.. In that case, this referral-based program can provide emergency rental assistance in Alaska. The resident must contact a participating Alaska Network on Domestic Violence and Sexual Assault member to be referred.Association of Alaska Housing AuthoritiesThe Association of Alaska Housing Authorities is a group that helps different communities throughout Alaska. It is working toward creating more safe and affordable housing solutions for residents. Many members also offer other services, including energy, weatherization, and home rehabilitation programs.Emergency Rental Assistance in Anchorage, AKMany programs discussed previously offer rental assistance in Anchorage, Alaska. However, one program in particular has yet to be addressed, and it provides many great assistance options to Anchorage residents. The Salvation Army: McKinnell House is located in Anchorage, AK, and offers emergency rental assistance, among many other programs. One such program is the Emergency Shelter for Homeless Families, which offers:24-hour stays.Nutritious meals.Case managementLifeskills developmentIn addition to emergency shelter, McKinnell House offers food and family services.CounselingResidents can talk to one of the counselors about life and spiritual issues. Spirituality is essential to The Salvation Army, which gives spiritual residents a place to go outside the church and be understood.Food BoxesResidents who are short on food can go to McKinnell House for prepared food boxes to help meet their nutritional needs. Residents and other organizations donate many of these items.Clothing VouchersThe Salvation Army receives clothing donations and hands out vouchers to needy families so they can shop for clothes. These clothes vary in size, so you can find what you need for anyone in the family.Utility AssistanceWith the severe weather conditions in Alaska, heat and electricity are essential. The Salvation Army McKinnel House offers utility assistance to avoid shut-off notices.Rental AssistanceAnother program The Salvation Army McKinnell House offers is emergency rental assistance in Anchorage, AK. You can ask for assistance if you need to catch up on rent or need help paying it.Find Emergency Rental Assistance in Alaska TodayIt is difficult to ask for help, especially when you need it, but there are solutions to your problems. There are numerous options for emergency rental assistance in Alaska. At Affordable Housing Hub, we make it easier to find what you need.

### Arizona Emergency Rental Assistance: 2025 Application Guide
Arizona is home to both desert land and vast forests. With a population of nearly 8 million residents, many options are available for emergency rental assistance in Arizona. Understanding the forms of help available and how to apply for Arizona emergency rental assistance is important.Arizona Emergency Rental AssistanceFinding and asking for help can be mentally and emotionally challenging. However, with the proper research, securing emergency rental assistance in Arizona can be easy.&nbsp;Arizona Department of Economic SecurityThe Arizona Department of Economic Security's goal is to assist individuals and families in need. They offer many programs to help Arizona communities, including:Food AssistanceThe food assistance program aims to help individuals with food security through several options.Supplemental Nutrition Assistance Program (SNAP).The Emergency Food Assistance Program (TEFAP).Commodity Senior Food Program (CSFP).WIC Farmers Markets Nutrition Program (FMNP).These are just a few of the food assistance options available. It is important to research each program and apply for the one that best fits your family's needs.Medical AssistanceThe Arizona Health Care Cost Containment System (AHCCCS) provides Medicaid insurance qualifying applicants based on income, Arizona residency, or pregnancy status to those in need. You can apply for this program online, in person, by mail, or by fax. When applying, make sure you have all the appropriate documentation, including but not limited to:Proof of citizenship for each applicant.Social Security Number for each applicant.Proof of all income for the household.Birth certificates for each applicant.Alien Registration CardsAfter you submit your application, a phone interview will be conducted to discuss the information you submitted and determine if any other documentation is needed.Arizona Rental Assistance ProgramThis emergency rental assistance program in Arizona is there to help low-income families with children and senior citizens avoid housing insecurity. To qualify for this program, you must meet specific criteria, including but not limited to:The applicant must be a tenant.Experiencing housing insecurity or eviction.Have a child under 18 in the home.A senior over 60 in the home.Other eligibility criteria apply, so make sure to do your research before applying. You can apply for the program online or in person.Low Income Home Energy Assistance ProgramThe Low Income Home Energy Assistance Program (LIHEAP) is available to low-income residents who need immediate help with utility bills. You can see if you qualify by taking the questionnaire on the website or by calling the phone number provided.Tempe Community Action AgencyThe Tempe Community Action Agency wants every person in the community to be happy and healthy. They aim to end poverty and help people secure safe, stable housing. They have many programs to help those in need, including:Food SecurityTempe, AZ, is home to one of the largest food pantries in the community. On certain days and times of the week, residents can visit the pantry and receive emergency food help twice a month. Bring your photo ID and proof of Tempe or Fountain Hills residency.Housing StabilityThe Tempe Community Action Agency offers multiple programs to help low-income families with utility assistance. Funds are available to residents working with select utility providers:Arizona Public Service (APS).Salt River Project (SRP).Southwest Gas.If you use one of the providers listed above, are low-income, and the crisis is emergent, help is available.Maricopa County Assistance ProgramsAs federal funding for Maricopa County’s Emergency Rental Assistance (ERA) program has ended, the county has formed new programs to help residents with their needs.&nbsp;Housing Stability Rental Assistance ProgramThe Housing Stability Rental Assistance program is an emergency rental assistance program in Arizona that helps low-income residents with up to 2 months of payments for past due rent payments, late fees, or future payments to keep them in stable, secure housing. To qualify for the program, you must meet specific criteria.Live in Maricopa County, except Glendale, Mesa, or Phoenix.Risk of homelessness, instability, or financial hardship.Income is 80% or less of the area median income.To establish eligibility, the resident must bring the proper documentation.Utility AssistanceThe Human Services Department’s Community Resilience Division helps Maricopa County residents with utility assistance. The applicant must live in Maricopa County, except Glendale, Mesa, and Phoenix, and income for the 30 days prior must be 60% or less of the state median income. You can apply online or in person.Coconino County Assistance ProgramsCoconino County also offers many programs to help residents, including help paying utility bills, rental assistance, vouchers for clothing, bus passes, food assistance, and more. Eligibility requirements may vary per program. However, consistent eligibility requirements include the number of people in the household, household income, and problems the household is experiencing.&nbsp;Find Emergency Rental Assistance Programs in ArizonaThere are many options available for emergency rental assistance in Arizona. At Affordable Housing Hub, we are dedicated to connecting you to the resources you need as you find the right solutions for your family.

### Arkansas Emergency Rental Assistance: 2025 Application Guide
COVID-19 changed the world and forced most of us to rely on others. The end of COVID-19 federal funding caused many of the emergency rental assistance programs in Arkansas to shut down, leaving many people with choices to make. However, numerous programs are still available to help Arkansas residents in their time of need.&nbsp;Central Delta Community Action AgencyOne option for emergency rental assistance in Arkansas is the Community Services Block Grant (CSBG) from the Central Delta Community Action Agency. The money a resident receives can be used for several issues they may face, including utility payments, rent payments, minor home repairs and appliances, car maintenance, or other issues approved by CSBG regulations. To quality, you must meet the following criteria:Proof of emergency.Be a resident of certain counties in Arkansas.125% or below the federal poverty line.Provide required documentation.The Central Delta Community Action Agency offers this program to empower low-income individuals and families by building stronger and healthier communities.Our Healthy CommunitiesThis non-profit community action agency provides numerous programs for Benton, Carroll, and Madison counties in Arkansas.&nbsp;WeatherizationThis program helps low-income families make their homes more efficient regarding utilities costs. A checklist is provided with the application so you have all the proper documentation before handing in your application. These requirements include but are not limited to:The completed weatherization application.Social Security award letter.Last four paystubs of anyone over 18.Completed lessor agreement if renting.They may require more information after reviewing your application.Water AssistanceThe cities of Rogers and Gravette partner with Our Healthy Communities to assist low-income families that need help paying their water bills to avoid shut-off. When applying for the program, you must submit the following information:Shut-off notice.Each member of the household's social security number.Each member of the household's birth date.Proof of household income.These items must be submitted so that your application can be filed correctly.Economic Opportunity AgencyThe Economic Opportunity Agency provides residents with The Emergency Food Assistance Program (TEFAP) to help low-income families with healthy food. They hope to provide healthy living alternatives to families within Arkansas.&nbsp;Partnering with Bread of Life in Springdale and LifeSource in Fayetteville, the Economic Opportunity Agency distributes food supplies and has a mobile food pantry.Community Action Program for Central ArkansasThe Community Action Program for Central Arkansas offers several special programs to families with incomes at or above 125% of the federal poverty level.The Community Blocks GrantThese grants include emergency medication assistance and emergency disaster assistance. Each program has its own application criteria. For example, the emergency medication assistance program does not provide narcotic or pain medication. For the emergency disaster assistance program, the resident must have a Red Cross Voucher, a referral, or a verifiable emergency.Emergency Solutions GrantThe Emergency Solutions Grant has four components, three of which do not have income requirements. It is aimed at individuals and families who are at risk or homeless.BRADThe Black River Area Development Corporation (BRAD) offers several emergency rental assistance programs in Arkansas. Both programs are provided to low—or very low-income individuals and families.Housing Choice Voucher ProgramThis program offers government-subsidized rental housing to qualifying low-income individuals and families. Applicants wait until assistance is available, during which they will be notified, given a voucher, and can start looking for a qualifying home. The house must meet the Housing Quality Standards for it to qualify.Home TBRA ProgramThis program is an extension of the Housing Choice Voucher Program, and applicants must meet the same criteria of being very low-income. Qualifying applicants will be housed in homes from the private market. Each home is recertified yearly according to the Housing Quality Standards rules and regulations.Crawford-Sabastian Community Development CouncilAn emergency rental assistance program in Arkansas is also available through Family Services at the Crawford-Sebastian Community Development Council. This rental assistance program is available on a first-come-first-serve basis to qualifying applicants. Individuals must meet income guidelines to be eligible for rental assistance help.Find Emergency Rental Assistance in Arkansas TodayEven though COVID-19 federal funding is over, assistance is still available. You can get help paying rent, finding housing, food, or utility assistance.

### California Emergency Rental Assistance: 2025 Application Guide
Realizing that rent will be due soon and you don’t have enough money to pay it is distressing. In California, the state gave out over $4 billion to help people make rent when times were tough during the COVID-19 pandemic. While that specific program is no longer available, if you need help from an emergency rental assistance program in California, you still have options.From Orange County to San Francisco County and everywhere in between, there are people who will help you keep a roof over your head and work toward a more financially secure future.CalWORKs California Emergency Rental Assistance ProgramThis program provides emergency rental assistance as well as support for food, utilities, and other essentials for California families in need. There is a welfare office that can help you apply for CalWORKs in every county. This program will give you cash aid that you can use for your most pressing needs – rent included.The amount of financial assistance you can get from CalWORKs is determined based on several factors, including:Whether your family includes people with special needs.How many people in your family are eligible based on income.Your overall household income.If your household includes children who have been deprived of support or care due to a parent’s absence, disability, or death.If your household’s principal earner is unemployed.If you’re curious whether or not your household qualifies for this program, you can contact your county’s Social Services for help.Emergency Rental Assistance in Orange County, CAOrange County offers its own emergency rental assistance programs tailored to the needs of its residents. This housing assistance is funded by the US US Department of Treasury and managed by local government. It aims to support low-income households that have been adversely affected by the pandemic.As with most local ERAP programs, services offered include rental assistance and utility payments to help keep people in their houses with functional services, such as water, electricity, gas, and more.To apply for the Orange County Emergency Rental Assistance Program (OC ERAP) you will need to apply through the Orange County Housing Authority online portal. Required documentation to receive assistance will include proof of your income, a copy of the rental agreement, and any evidence you can provide related to proving your financial hardship and relationship to the pandemic.Riverside County Housing Support ProgramThis program is available to Riverside County residents who are struggling to make rent. The Housing Support Program can be used in addition to support from CalWORKs to help Riverside residents afford all of their basic needs.Whether you’re concerned about an upcoming rent payment or already close to eviction, this Housing Support Program can help you make ends meet. You can find out if your household qualifies by getting in touch with them via email at hsp@rivco.org or via phone call at 833-391-0506.Rental Assistance Programs in San Diego CountyThe Housing Authority of the County of San Diego (HACSD) offers a multitude of rental assistance options depending on your unique circumstances. You may qualify for assistance if you earn less than 50% of the median income in your area, even if that wouldn’t qualify as low income in other areas.&nbsp;Housing Opportunities for Persons With AIDSThis program provides housing assistance to people living with HIV and AIDS. If you or anyone in your household have AIDS or HIV and are low income, make sure you check the box for Housing Opportunities for Persons with AIDS (HOPWA) when you apply for rental assistance.Veterans Affairs Supportive HousingThis program provides rental assistance to qualified homeless veterans. If you are already behind on rent and facing eviction, and you or anyone in your household are a military veteran, this program may be able to help you avoid homelessness and get back on your feet.Income-Based Rental AssistanceIf you qualify based on income but don’t have any veterans or AIDS and HIV patients in your household, you can still apply for the San Diego County income-based rental assistance program. The highest priority for these programs goes to residents with:Elderly household membersDisabled household membersJobs that have them working 32+ hours per weekA history of homelessnessDependent childrenEven if you don’t meet the criteria for highest priority, however, you can still receive assistance based on income. You can find out if you qualify by applying for rental assistance.Other Local Emergency Rental Assistance Programs in CaliforniaAs a vast and diverse state, California offers many different rental assistance programs, which vary based on jurisdiction. Some of the largest, and therefore most impactful programs include those based in Los Angeles, San Diego, San Francisco, and Riverside counties. The specific agency handling cases in each region can vary depending on the structure of the local government.&nbsp;Los Angeles County Development AuthoritySan Francisco Human Services Agency.City of Palmade Tenant-Based Rental AssistanceIf you’re not sure where to look for help in your county, you can use the Affordable Housing Hub search page to find the programs available in your area.Finding and Accessing the Right Program for YouNavigating all the details of getting into an emergency rental assistant program can be challenging. However, California’s emergency rental programs offer vital support for anyone who is facing a time of financial hardship.&nbsp;Whether you are in a major city or a small town, help is available. Document your situation, follow application instructions carefully, and remember that these programs are designed to keep you and your family safe and housed. If you need help figuring out the right next step, reach out to your local agency and get help today.

### Colorado Emergency Rental Assistance: 2024 Application Guide
The COVID-19 Pandemic has had lasting effects on the economy and housing. Colorado’s emergency rental assistance programs aim to provide financial relief to tenants struggling to make ends meet and pay their rent. These initiatives are supported by federal, state, and local funds and are administered through various agencies and organizations to ensure broad reach and accessibility.The Emergency Rental Assistance Program (ERAP)A primary resource for Colorado residents is the Emergency Rental Assistance Program (ERAP). Funded by the U.S. Treasury, ERAP provides substantial support to renters facing financial hardships due to the pandemic. The program covers up to 15 months of rent and utility payments, including arrears and future payments, offering critical relief for those most in need.To qualify for ERAP, applicants must meet these specific criteria:Household income must be at or below 80% of the Area Median Income (AMI).Applicants must demonstrate a financial hardship directly or indirectly related to COVID-19.Proof of residency and a valid lease agreement are required.The application process involves submitting an online application along with necessary documentation such as income verification, proof of rental arrears, and identification. Both tenants and landlords can apply, facilitating a collaborative effort to secure housing stability.Colorado Emergency Housing Assistance Program (EHAP)The Colorado Emergency Housing Assistance Program (EHAP), administered by the Colorado Division of Housing, provides another layer of support. EHAP is designed to assist renters who have lost income due to the pandemic and are at risk of eviction.EHAP has similar eligibility criteria to ERAP, focusing on households experiencing financial hardship due to COVID-19. The application process requires documentation of income loss, proof of tenancy, and the amount of rent owed. Applications can be submitted online, and local agencies are available to assist applicants through the process.Local Assistance ProgramsIn addition to state-administered programs, various municipalities in Colorado offer local rental assistance programs. These programs cater to specific community needs and often provide more tailored support.Denver's Temporary Rental and Utility Assistance (TRUA)Denver’s Temporary Rental and Utility Assistance (TRUA) program offers short-term financial assistance to low- and moderate-income residents facing unexpected financial hardship. TRUA can cover up to six months of rent and utility payments.City of Aurora Rental Assistance ProgramIf you need emergency rental assistance in Aurora CO the city offers a program through House Aurora Partnership. The program uses CARES Act funding from Arapahoe and Adams counties. More information is available through Arapahoe county.Boulder County Housing HelplineBoulder County operates a Housing Helpline that connects residents to emergency rental assistance, housing counseling, and other supportive services. This helpline is a valuable resource for residents navigating housing instability and seeking immediate support.El Paso County's Rent Assistance ProgramEl Paso County’s Rent Assistance Program provides targeted aid to residents at risk of eviction. The program collaborates with local nonprofits and community organizations to offer comprehensive support, including financial aid and case management services.Eviction Prevention and Legal AssistancePreventing evictions is a critical component of Colorado’s housing stability efforts. Several organizations provide legal assistance, mediation services, and counseling to help tenants facing eviction proceedings.Colorado Legal ServicesColorado Legal Services offers free legal aid to low-income residents, helping them understand their rights and navigate eviction processes. This organization plays a crucial role in representing tenants in court and negotiating with landlords.Mediation ServicesMediation programs, such as those provided by the Denver County Court, offer an alternative to eviction by facilitating negotiations between tenants and landlords. These services aim to reach mutually agreeable solutions and keep tenants in their homes.Housing CounselingNonprofits like Brothers Redevelopment, Inc. provide housing counseling to assist tenants with budgeting, understanding their rights, and finding alternative housing options if necessary. These services are essential for maintaining long-term housing stability.The Critical Impact of Rental Assistance ProgramsEmergency rental assistance programs have had a profound impact on Colorado communities. By providing financial relief, these programs help prevent evictions, reduce homelessness, and support economic stability. A study by the Urban Institute indicates that rental assistance not only keeps families housed but also enables them to focus on other critical areas such as employment, education, and health.Challenges and Future DirectionsDespite their successes, rental assistance programs face challenges such as funding limitations, bureaucratic hurdles, and the need for ongoing support. Colorado policymakers and housing advocates are working to address these challenges by advocating for additional funding, simplifying application procedures, and increasing outreach to ensure that all eligible residents can access these vital resources.Getting Emergency Rental Assistance in ColoradoEmergency rental assistance programs in Colorado are essential in supporting residents facing housing insecurity. As these programs continue to evolve, ongoing advocacy and policy innovation will be key to addressing the housing crisis and building a resilient future for all Colorado residents. For more information, see our overview on what to do when you’re struggling to pay rent and learn about other sources of help.

### Connecticut Emergency Rental Assistance: 2024 Application Guide
There are several emergency rental assistance programs in Connecticut for residents who struggle with housing insecurity. This challenge is common, especially after the economic disruptions caused by the COVID-19 pandemic.&nbsp;Overview of Emergency Rental Assistance ProgramsConnecticut offers several emergency rental assistance programs designed to prevent evictions and homelessness. These programs are usually funded by federal, state, and local sources. This includes the U.S. Treasury's Emergency Rental Assistance Program (ERAP). The Connecticut Department of Housing (DOH) and local agencies administer them and aim to provide timely help to renters in need.UniteCT ProgramOne flagship program in Connecticut is UniteCT. It's a state-run program that gives federal funds to help households that can't pay rent and utilities due to the pandemic. UniteCT provides up to $15,000 in rental assistance and up to $1,500 for electric utilities per household. This financial aid covers both past-due and future rent. It offers a critical lifeline for struggling renters.To qualify for UniteCT, applicants must meet the following criteria:Household income must be at or below 80% of the Area Median Income (AMI).Applicants must demonstrate financial hardship due to COVID-19.Proof of residency and a valid lease agreement are required.The application process is straightforward but requires thorough documentation. Applicants must fill out an online form and also submit income verification and evidence of rental arrears. Landlords are also encouraged to join.&nbsp;Eviction Prevention ServicesIn addition to direct rental assistance, Connecticut offers several eviction prevention services. The Eviction Prevention Fund provides legal aid, mediation programs, and housing counseling to help tenants who are facing eviction.Legal AssistanceOrganizations like Connecticut Legal Services and the New Haven Legal Assistance Association provide free legal help to low-income renters. These agencies help tenants understand their rights and represent them in court and negotiate with landlords to find friendly solutions.Mediation ProgramsThe Connecticut Fair Housing Center provides renters with critical mediation services. Mediation plays a key role in resolving disputes between landlords and tenants. Mediation provides a platform for both parties to discuss their issues with a neutral third party. The goal is to reach a settlement that stops eviction.Housing CounselingNon-profit organizations like the Connecticut Housing Finance Authority (CHFA) offer housing counseling services. These experienced counselors offer personalized advice that covers topics like budgeting, tenant rights, and finding new housing if needed.Local Assistance ProgramsBeyond state-administered initiatives, many municipalities in Connecticut offer their own rental assistance programs. These local programs have more flexible rules and can also provide additional help to residents not covered by state or federal programs.Hartford's Emergency Assistance FundHartford has set up an Emergency Assistance Fund to help residents who do not qualify for UniteCT or need immediate help. This fund offers short-term financial assistance to prevent evictions and stabilize housing situations.New Haven's Rental Assistance ProgramNew Haven provides a rental assistance program focused on low-income families and individuals. This program works with local non-profits and community organizations to provide full support, including money and help in finding housing.Rental Assistance Programs and the CommunityEmergency rental programs have helped thousands of residents in Connecticut and had a big impact on communities. These programs provide financial relief and prevent evictions keeping residents in their neighborhoods. This helps keep communities stable and reduces the strain on homeless shelters and social services.A recent analysis by the U.S. Department of the Treasury highlighted the impact of the Emergency Rental Assistance (ERA) program, which has provided over $46 billion to support housing stability for eligible renters throughout the COVID-19 pandemic. The program has made over 10 million assistance payments, significantly helping low-income renters and renters of color. Research shows that the ERA program has played a crucial role in preventing evictions, with more than 80% of ERA assistance in 2021 going to very low-income households.Challenges and Future DirectionsDespite the successes, rental assistance programs face challenges like bureaucratic delays, limited funding, and the need for ongoing support. The pandemic's economic effects linger and there is a growing need for steady funding and simpler processes to ensure that help reaches those in need quickly.Connecticut policymakers and housing advocates are continuously working to improve these programs. We are trying to increase outreach, to simplify applications, and secure more funding from federal and state sources.Finding Emergency Rental Assistance in ConnecticutNo one wants to feel helpless about paying their rent. The Connecticut emergency rental assistance program that existed during the pandemic may be gone, but that should not be a barrier to confidently supporting your housing situation.&nbsp;Whether you’re seeking emergency rental assistance in Hartford, CT, or looking for help in Fairfield County, you are never far from the aid you need. For more information regarding rental assistance programs, check out our overview for those struggling to pay rent.

### Delaware Emergency Rental Assistance: 2024 Application Guide
With the cost of living on the rise, many individuals and families are in need of an emergency rental assistance program. Delaware offers programs and resources to help residents maintain stable housing and avoid eviction.&nbsp;Emergency rental assistance programs in Delaware help ensure that individuals and families can stay in their homes during times of financial hardship. This guide provides an overview of the various programs and resources available across the state of Delaware in 2024.Emergency Assistance FundsThe state of Delaware provides emergency assistance funds to help low-income Delaware residents cover the cost of rent and utilities. Individuals and families seeking emergency assistance funds from the state of Delaware must:Receive or be eligible for cash assistance such as Temporary Assistance for Needy Families (TANF), General Assistance (GA), Supplemental Security Income (SSI), or certain Medicaid programs.&nbsp;Show that the housing emergency was the result of unforeseen circumstances that were outside the recipients’ control.Be able to maintain their housing after the emergency is addressed.This program aims to provide a safety net for residents who are facing temporary setbacks, ensuring they do not lose their homes due to circumstances beyond their control.Eviction Defense ProjectFacing eviction can be a daunting and stressful experience. Delaware residents who are facing eviction can consult the resources provided by the Eviction Defense Project. These resources include legal aid as well as financial support to keep Delaware residents housed. Legal aid services can help residents understand their rights and navigate the eviction process, potentially preventing displacement.The Eviction Defense Project is an essential resource for those who need immediate assistance and advice. By providing both legal and financial support, the project helps residents avoid eviction and stabilize their living situations.New Castle County ResourcesIndividuals and families seeking emergency rental assistance in New Castle County can visit one of the following service centers to confirm their eligibility and apply:&nbsp;Appoquinimink State Service Center (Middletown)Belvedere State Service Center (Wilmington)Claymont State Service CenterDeLaWarr State Service Center (New Castle)Floyd I. Hudson State Service Center (Newark)Northeast State Service Center (Wilmington)Winder Laird Porter State Service Center (Wilmington)These centers provide a range of services and support to ensure residents can access the help they need promptly. Each center is equipped to handle applications and provide guidance on the emergency assistance funds available.Kent County ResourcesIndividuals and families seeking emergency rental assistance in Kent County can visit one of the following service centers to confirm their eligibility and apply:James W. Williams State Service Center (Dover)Smyrna State Service Center (Smyrna)Kent County's service centers are dedicated to helping residents in need of emergency assistance. The staff at these centers can help applicants understand the requirements and complete their applications efficiently.Sussex County ResourcesIndividuals and families seeking emergency rental assistance in Sussex County can visit one of the following service centers to confirm their eligibility and apply:Bridgeville State Service CenterEdward W. Pyle State Service Center (Frankford)Laurel State Service CenterThurman Adams State Service Center (formerly the Georgetown State Service Center)Anna C. Shipley State Service Center (Seaford)Sussex County offers multiple locations where residents can seek help. Each center provides personalized assistance to ensure that every applicant receives the support they need.Milford ResourcesIndividuals and families seeking emergency rental assistance can visit one of the following service centers in Milford to confirm their eligibility and apply:&nbsp;Milford State Service CenterMilford Walnut Street BuildingMilford's service centers are strategically located to serve the community efficiently. These centers are vital for residents who need immediate help with rental assistance.Non-Profit Organizations and Community GroupsIn addition to the resources mentioned above, several non-profit organizations and community groups offer support and guidance to those facing housing insecurity. These groups often provide supplemental assistance and can help residents connect with additional services such as food banks, job training programs, and financial counseling.Further HelpNavigating the complexities of emergency rental assistance can be challenging, but Delaware offers a robust network of resources to support residents in need. Whether you are facing eviction or simply struggling to make ends meet, there are programs and organizations ready to help. By reaching out to local service centers and utilizing available resources, Delaware residents can find the support they need to maintain stable and secure housing.If you’re struggling to pay rent, check out Affordable Housing Hub’s overview of resources. This page provides information on resources available across the United States for people experiencing housing emergencies. You can also visit the Delaware State Housing Authority website for more information on emergency rental assistance programs.&nbsp;

### Florida Emergency Rental Assistance: 2024 Application Guide
In Florida, emergency rental assistance programs saw closures and rollbacks across all counties in 2023. This removed some access points to rental assistance that were available to many Floridians at the height of the COVID-19 pandemic. However, if you are in need of emergency rental assistance, Florida still offers several options.
Temporary Cash Assistance (TCA)Florida’s Temporary Cash Assistance Program (TCA) provides financial support to individuals and families with minor children who need a bit of a boost. This program provides monthly cash assistance payments to qualifying Floridians for up to a lifetime total of 48 months. Families can receive extra income from this program based on the number of children currently living in the home, as well as the age(s) of said child(ren).&nbsp;To receive TCA funding, individuals and families must provide evidence that they make less than 185% of the current Federal Poverty level. There are several other criteria that applicants must meet, including:Possession of a Social Security Number, or proof that applicants have applied for one.Proof of residence in the state of Florida.Proof of work activities, in some cases.Countable assets totalling to equal or less than $2,000.Up to date immunizations for children under age 5.More information about TCA can be found on the Fact Sheet compiled by the Florida Department of Children and Families.Temporary Assistance for Needy Families (TANF)The Temporary Assistance for Needy Families (TANF) program was first put in place in Florida in 1996. Since then, the program has helped countless families in need, and it has been so productive that it recently earned renewal through 2026.The TANF program offers monetary assistance to families that the state of Florida deems “needy.” in order to fall into this category, families must meet many of the same criteria as those applying for TCA. However, TANF eligibility is more flexible for those who lose TCA eligibility due to employment, or for two-parent homes that may not fully meet TCA requirements. In addition, Floridians who are 18 years of age or younger and who are heads of household may qualify for additional assistance through TANF.As with other programs, applicants must be residents of Florida to receive benefits and must sometimes provide proof of work or employment, if possible.&nbsp;Emergency Solutions GrantIf you are currently homeless, or actively facing homelessness, you may consider pursuing assistance from the Emergency Solutions Grant. Supported by the U.S. Department of Housing and Urban Development, this grant funds, among other things, rental assistance programs and shelter locations for those affected by homelessness.If you are currently under threat of homelessness, or have recently become homeless, you can access any relevant resources and funding through your local Continuum of Care.What are Continuums of Care?In Florida, Continuums of Care (CoCs) are local networks of organizations involved in providing a range of services. These groups can include homeless services providers, public housing agencies, school districts, and many others. All CoCs are constructed with the goal of locating and supporting homeless individuals in their areas and putting them back on the path to stable housing.All CoCs are unique to different areas of Florida. Be sure to reach out to the CoC that is most relevant to your location.Section 8 HousingHousing assistance from the state is not the only housing assistance option in Florida. Section 8 housing, the federal government’s most widely-known housing assistance program, is available throughout the state of Florida.&nbsp;Section 8 housing is often commended for its flexibility in applicable housing situations. Those eligible for Section 8 vouchers can choose to live in single-family homes, apartments, townhomes, and the like. As with TCA and TANF, Floridians must demonstrate appropriate financial need in order to qualify for participation in Section 8.All Section 8 housing is coordinated through local Public Housing Agencies (PHAs). These groups are dedicated to pairing affordable housing with individuals in need. To find your nearest PHA, use our simple Search Tool.Finding Rental Assistance in FloridaNo one wants to feel helpless about paying their rent. The Florida emergency rental assistance program that existed during the pandemic may be gone, but that should not be a barrier to confidently supporting your housing situation. Whether you’re seeking emergency rental assistance in Jacksonville, FL, or looking for help in Santa Rosa County, you are never far from the aid you need.For more information regarding rental assistance programs, check out our overview for those struggling to pay rent.

### Georgia Emergency Rental Assistance: 2025 Application Guide
Individuals and families can be struck by hardship at any time leaving them at risk of eviction from their homes. The problem was aggravated even more by the COVID-19 pandemic, where millions of people across the country faced financial difficulty and pre-existing housing inequalities were magnified. Emergency rental assistance programs in Georgia are one way to make sure those in need get necessary help.&nbsp;These programs are meant to assist those facing hard times by paying all or a portion of their monthly rent and/or utilities for a specified time. The criteria for these programs vary: assisting those who meet a certain income threshold, who live in a particular county or zip code, family demographics, or those who fall into a specific age bracket.&nbsp;Find out how emergency rental assistance programs in Georgia work and whether you may qualify.&nbsp;Housing Choice Voucher ProgramThe Georgia Department of Community Affairs (DCA) runs the Housing Choice Voucher (HCV) program. Formerly known as Section 8, this program is a tenant-based rental assistance program for low-income individuals and families, as well as older adults and people with disabilities, to rent safe and affordable dwellings.&nbsp;The HCV is meant to provide&nbsp; improved living environments and fair housing for low-income residents. Upon applying and having an application approved, the DCA provides subsidy payments directly to the property owners on behalf of the program participants.&nbsp;The HCV is administered in 149 of Georgia’s 159 counties. The DCA does not have jurisdiction in the remaining counties and similar programs are administered through their housing authority.&nbsp;Applying for the HCV program involves filling out an application and submitting the required documents. Applicants are placed on a waitlist and then selected from a lottery to verify eligibility.&nbsp;Local Rental Assistance Programs in GeorgiaIn addition to federally funded programs, The State of Georgia also offers emergency rental assistance on a local level. These agencies deliver rental assistance and other services to residents based on their county, city, or zip code. Organizations include:&nbsp;Midtown Assistance Center, Inc.&nbsp;With the Midtown Assistance Center, Inc., people living in certain zip codes and who have consistently paid the total amount of rent they owe over the last six months can receive help on rent and utilities. Applicants must also have been consistently employed over the last six months, or recently unemployed, and show sufficient income for future months’ bills.Star-C Corporation Eviction Diversion Program&nbsp;This program, servicing people living in the City of Atlanta, covers up to $7,000 in rent to those in the city experiencing hardship due to job loss or reduction of hours, or emergencies such as transportation or medical emergencies.Action, Inc.&nbsp;People living in Athens-Clarke, Barrow, Elbert, Greene, Jackson, Madison, Morgan, Oconee,&nbsp; Oglethorpe and Walton Counties may be eligible to receive assistance with rent or utilities from Action, Inc. Their Community Services program helps those who have experienced financial hardship within the last 90 days. Applicants can receive assistance one time in a 24-month period.&nbsp;&nbsp;Neighborhood Cooperative MinistriesNeighborhood Cooperative Ministries provides rent and utility assistance to at-risk Gwinnett County residents from Doraville, Norcross, Peachtree Corners, and Tucker as well as Greater Gwinnett through community partner referrals and funding cycles. Call or visit their office to get started.&nbsp;County governments or other local agencies throughout Georgia may administer their own rental assistance programs outside of state or federally funded initiatives. Check with your municipality to find out what their rental assistance options are and how you can qualify.&nbsp;Other ProgramsCertain initiatives are administered through the U.S. Department of Housing and Urban Development (HUD). These include the HCV program as well as a subsidized apartments program where apartment owners are assisted by HUD in providing reduced rent prices to low-income tenants. HUD also runs the HOME program, which gives grants to state and local governments to provide affordable housing.&nbsp;&nbsp;Finally, the GA/RYSE program is aimed at helping young adults get on their feet with household startup costs. They can provide temporary rental assistance for up to three months as well as utility and rental deposits, food services, and coaching assistance with an approved living plan. Eligibility depends on age, whether you're a post-secondary student, and if you're "in care" or "out of care.”Finding Rental Assistance in GeorgiaIf you or someone you know in Georgia have come upon hard times and are in need of rental assistance, help is available. Use our Affordable Housing Search to get in touch with your local agency and learn more about your options.&nbsp;

### Hawaii Emergency Rental Assistance: 2025 Application Guide
The COVID-19 pandemic and the Maui wildfires have left many Hawaii residents struggling to find the financial resources they need to cover the cost of housing. If you’re worried about making past, current, or future rent payments for your household, there are emergency rental assistance programs in Hawaii that can help you.Statewide Emergency Rental Assistance in HawaiiThere are currently 2 statewide emergency rental assistance programs available in Hawaii: the DHS Rental Assistance Program and the OHA’s Ka Wailele Emergency Financial Assistance Program. To help you determine if these programs may be of assistance to you, let’s break down the details of each one, including how you can apply.DHS Rental Assistance for Wildfire SurvivorsIn December 2023, the State of Hawaii Department of Human Services (DHS) announced the DHS Rental Assistance Program specifically for survivors of the Maui wildfires who did not qualify for assistance from the Federal Emergency Management Agency (FEMA). The program provides housing through Airbnb or the Hawaii Housing Finance and Development Corporation (HHFDC) Hawaii Fire Relief Housing Program.Eligible households can receive housing for up to 12 months and will pay an average monthly rate depending on the number of bedrooms in the property:0-1 Bedroom: $5,000/month2 bedrooms: $7,000/month3 bedrooms: $9,000/month4 bedrooms: $11,000/monthDHS, GEM, or the American Red Cross will contact most households that qualify for support, but you can apply separately by emailing hawaii@globalempowermentmission.org if you believe your household may be eligible.OHA’s Ka Wailele Emergency Financial Assistance ProgramThe Ka Wailele Emergency Financial Assistance Program offers financial assistance to Native Hawaiians who are 18 years or older and struggling with financial hardships. Awards can range from $1,500 to $2,000 and can cover expenses like rent, mortgage, utility support, car repairs, funeral expenses, and out-of-pocket medical expenses.Applicants do not have to meet certain income requirements to be eligible for the program. However, participants can only receive assistance once every 2 years.To stay updated on the program’s status, you can sign up to receive updates from the Office of Hawaiian Affairs (OHA).Hawaii County Emergency Rental Assistance ProgramThe Hawaii County Emergency Rental Assistance Program can help residents of Hawaii County cover the cost of past due rent, prospective rent, and rental deposits. Any past due payments between April 2020 and current day are eligible for up to 18 months total of assistance.To be eligible for the program, you must be a Hawaii County resident who is at least 18 years old and can provide proof of:Financial hardship or risk of homelessness or housing instabilityLate rent, eviction notice, or homelessnessHousehold income limits at or below 80% AMIHere are the estimated annual income limits for different sized households:1 member: $56,5002 members: $64,5503 members: $72,6004 members: $80,6505 members: $87,1506 members: $93,6007 members: $100,0508 members: $106,500Eligible households can apply now through the website or call the phone line for assistance at 808-298-5566.Maui County Emergency Rental Assistance ProgramThe Maui County Emergency Rental Assistance Program helps low-income households that have been financially impacted by the COVID-19 pandemic pay their rent, utility bills, or both. Eligible households can receive up to 12 months of assistance with payments made directly to the specific landlord or utility.For past due payments, the program will cover bills going back to March 13, 2020 at a rate of $2,500 per month. The support for current and future bills is $2,000 per month for rent and up to $500 per month for utilities.Only new applicants can currently apply for the pre-screening process.KHAKO Rental Assistance ProgramThe KHAKO Rental Assistance Program is a comprehensive homelessness prevention program that provides both rental assistance payments and counseling and case management to Maui residents. Those eligible to receive support are individuals and families moving from emergency shelter to permanent housing and those who are homeless or at risk of becoming homeless due to a lack of financial resources.Participants in the program can receive assistance with:Past rent.Security deposits.First month’s rent.Utility deposit or disconnection.You must complete a pre-application screening before submitting your full application. For extra assistance, you can reach a Rental Assistance Coordinator at (808) 446-8129.Emergency Rental Assistance for EveryoneNo matter where you live in Hawaii, you should be able to receive financial support for your housing, especially in times of emergency. For more information about emergency rental assistance in Hawaii and other states, check out our complete guide to rental assistance programs.

### Idaho Emergency Rental Assistance: 2025 Application Guide
As the cost of living continues to increase, many individuals and families need help paying for their Idaho housing. Emergency rental assistance programs play a pivotal role in helping Idaho residents avoid eviction and stay housed during challenging economic times. If you’re having trouble paying your rent in Idaho, here is an guide to the Idaho emergency rental assistance that is available to you.Temporary Assistance for Families in Idaho (TAFI)One resource available across the state of Idaho is the Temporary Assistance for Families in Idaho (TAFI) Program. TAFI provides short-term financial assistance to low-income families. This assistance can be critical in covering rent and other necessary expenses, helping families avoid homelessness. The program aims to promote self-sufficiency by providing support while families work towards improving their financial situation through employment and education.Idaho Legal AidIdaho individuals and families who are facing eviction may need legal support to navigate the situation and remain housed. Idaho Legal Aid Services, Inc. is a non-profit organization that provides free legal services to low-income and senior citizen Idaho residents. This organization helps tenants understand their rights, negotiate with landlords, and if necessary, represent them in court. Legal support can be crucial in preventing unjust evictions and ensuring that all legal procedures are properly followed.Idaho Housing Information Referral CenterIdaho residents can contact the Idaho Housing Information Referral Center to speak with a counselor about emergency housing options. The counselors can provide information on available rental assistance programs, help residents find affordable housing, and offer guidance on managing housing costs. This service is an invaluable resource for those who are unsure where to turn for help and need immediate advice on their housing situation.Benewah, Bonner, Boundary, Kootenai, and Shoshone Emergency Rental AssistanceIdaho Individuals and families looking for emergency rental assistance in Benewah, Bonner, Boundary, Kootenai, or Shoshone can contact St. Vincent de Paul, which is a non-profit organization that provides support for Idaho residents in need. Services include emergency shelters as well as financial assistance to help cover the cost of rent and utilities. St. Vincent de Paul also offers case management services to assist individuals in finding long-term solutions to their housing challenges, ensuring sustained support beyond immediate financial aid.Clearwater, Idaho County, Latah, Lewis, and Nez Perce Emergency Rental AssistanceIdahoans seeking emergency rental assistance in Clearwater, Idaho County, Latah, Lewis, or Nez Perce can reach out to the local Salvation Army. Among its other services, the Salvation Army helps people find and maintain safe and affordable housing. They offer various forms of support, including emergency financial assistance, shelter services, and transitional housing programs. The organization’s holistic approach ensures that individuals and families receive the comprehensive help they need to achieve housing stability.Ada, Adams, Boise, Canyon, Elmore, Gem, Owyhee, Payette, Valley, and Washington Emergency Rental AssistanceFor veterans and their families in Ada, Adams, Boise, Canyon, Elmore, Gem, Owyhee, Payette, Valley, and Washington, the Support Services for Veteran Families (SSVF) Program provides case management services to help participants receive public assistance. SSVF also provides financial assistance for expenses such as rent, utilities, and rental application fees. The program focuses on preventing homelessness among veterans by offering tailored support that addresses their unique needs and challenges.All Idahoans in Ada, Adams, Boise, Canyon, Elmore, Gem, Owyhee, Payette, Valley, and Washington can contact Jesse Tree for case management as well as financial assistance for expenses such as rent. Jesse Tree works closely with individuals and families to create sustainable housing plans, offering not just immediate financial relief but also long-term solutions to ensure ongoing housing stability.Blaine, Camas, Cassia, Gooding, Jerome, Lincoln, Minidoka, and Twin Falls Emergency Rental AssistanceResidents of Blaine, Camas, Cassia, Gooding, Jerome, Lincoln, Minidoka, and Twin Falls can contact the South Central Community Action Partnership for financial assistance with rent and utilities. This organization provides a range of services aimed at reducing poverty and improving the quality of life for residents. They offer emergency assistance as well as programs designed to promote self-sufficiency and long-term financial stability.Bannock, Bear Lake, Bingham, Caribou, Franklin, Oneida, and Power Emergency Rental AssistanceIdahoans in Bannock, Bear Lake, Bingham, Caribou, Franklin, Oneida, or Power can contact Aid for Friends for information on emergency shelter services. Aid for Friends provides temporary housing solutions, meals, and other support services for individuals and families experiencing homelessness. Their goal is to help people transition from emergency shelters to stable, permanent housing.Bonneville, Butte, Clark, Custer, Fremont, Jefferson, Lemhi, Madison, Teton Emergency Rental AssistanceClub, Inc. provides affordable housing for Idahoans in Bonneville, Butte, Clark, Custer, Fremont, Jefferson, Lemhi, Madison, and Teton. They offer various housing programs, including emergency rental assistance, to ensure that residents have access to safe and affordable housing options. Their services are designed to support individuals and families in achieving and maintaining housing stability.County Government ProgramsDepending on the availability of funds, individual counties in Idaho may offer emergency rental assistance. These programs can vary in terms of eligibility requirements and the types of assistance provided. To learn more about what your county offers and see if you qualify, visit your county’s website. Local government programs can be a crucial source of support for residents facing financial difficulties.Learn More About Idaho Emergency Rental AssistanceIf you’re struggling to keep up with the cost of your Idaho housing, emergency rental assistance is available. The state government, local governments, and several non-profit organizations offer Idaho emergency rental assistance. These programs are designed to provide immediate financial relief and support, helping residents avoid eviction and maintain stable housing. For more information on programs that can help you with housing expenses, visit Idaho Housing.

### Illinois Emergency Rental Assistance: 2025 Application Guide
The cost of housing in Illinois has risen significantly in recent years. In urban areas like Chicago, Champagne, and Rockford, affordable rental living is difficult to come by. Nonetheless, the population of these areas has continued to grow, and so has the demand for housing. Because of this, there are a variety of Illinois emergency rental assistance programs available for state residents who may be struggling with increased rent prices.During times of emergency or financial hardship, many Americans find themselves at risk of being evicted. The cost of housing isn’t going down any time soon. Fortunately, there are short-term options available for Illinoisans who find themselves struggling to make rent. The state of Illinois provides emergency rental assistance for those who are in financial crisis and at risk of homelessness.&nbsp;Illinois Emergency Rental Assistance Program Requirements&nbsp;Each rental assistance program will have different requirements, but you may be eligible for emergency assistance if you find yourself in an emergency situation, for example:&nbsp;You recently became unemployed and do not have a stable incomeYou are currently waiting on an eviction court case and are struggling to make rentYou have experienced significant financial hardship due to the COVID-19 pandemic and its aftermathYour current income is at or below 80% of the area median income&nbsp;There are many extenuating circumstances that can make paying rent difficult. Below are some state-specific aid programs.&nbsp;&nbsp;Illinois Rental AssistanceThe major rental assistance program in the state is the Illinois Court-based Rental Assistance program. If you are a tenant who is facing eviction but has a pending case in court, you may be eligible for state rent assistance. Proof of citizenship is not a requirement for this form of aid.&nbsp;Cash assistance programs in Illinois may be able to help your family stay afloat and keep your rental home during a time of financial crisis. For example, TANF can help pay for food, shelter, and other necessities.&nbsp;Region-Specific ResourcesAs the greater Chicago area has the highest population density and the highest rate of homelessness, it is one of the most expensive cities in the United States. Funding dedicated to rental assistance is available, particularly for those most impacted by the pandemic. The Chicago Rental Assistance program is available to all Chicago residents who meet the income requirements and are at risk of eviction, regardless of citizenship status. Visit the application portal for more information.There’s emergency rental assistance in Rockford, IL through their Community Action Assistance Program helps people with their first month of rent in a new location and provides temporary shelter for those who are already homeless.&nbsp;The Champagne County Habitat for Humanities program can guide families to further housing assistance resources and help with rent assistance applications. The City of Champagne Township also provides general social assistance, which also applies to housing.&nbsp;Nonprofits, Local Churches, and Private OrganizationsState-based options may not be easily accessible to everyone. Another way to receive rental assistance is by working with nonprofit organizations or local churches. These types of organizations tend to have less “red tape” in the way of accessing rental assistance, but they also have limited resources and can only help each individual case to a certain extent.Often, these organizations have a specific mission or community that they serve, such as:Domestic violence sheltersHousing for immigrants and refugees&nbsp;Housing for people with a disability&nbsp;Housing for people suffering from addiction&nbsp;These programs may offer temporary housing solutions including rent assistance.&nbsp;Sometimes, private organizations such as banks or nonprofits can provide small loans to those who need temporary cash assistance for rent. Charity organizations often provide assistance with flexible requirements for paying the money back. Whatever your immediate needs are, there are a variety of emergency rental assistance programs in Illinois to help you get back on your feet.Frequently Asked QuestionsFor how long can I receive rent assistance?Most programs only provide assistance for a few months at a time. Emergency rent assistance is designed for those who are experiencing a temporary crisis that makes them unable to pay their rent for the time being.&nbsp;What if I need housing assistance for a longer period of time?For longer-term housing assistance visit the Affordable Housing Hub to explore options in finding affordable housing.For Illinois residents, it is also a good idea to visit the Illinois Department of Human Services to explore resources.&nbsp;How long does it take to receive rent assistance?Depending on the type of program you are applying for, receiving aid can take. It is also never guaranteed that you will receive emergency rent assistance as funding is almost always limited, so it is important to start the process as soon as possible.&nbsp;Facing housing insecurity is frightening and navigating social aid is not easy. At Affordable Housing Hub, we are here to support you in your path to stable housing.

### Indiana Emergency Rental Assistance: 2025 Application Guide
It's no secret that rent in Indiana has gone up significantly in the past few years. If you are a part of the one-third of Hoosiers who rent a living space, it is possible that you may at some point find yourself in an emergency situation in which you need help making rent. Fortunately, there are several Indiana emergency rental assistance programs out there to help.Particularly in the years during and following the COVID-19 pandemic, countless renters have found themselves in situations of financial instability that put them in danger of homelessness. It’s important to be familiar with rental assistance options available in your community so that you can act quickly when you or someone you know needs help.Indiana Emergency Rental AssistanceThe Indiana state government offers several different programs to help tenants pay rent and maintain safe, stable housing. Here are a few of the programs that your household may want to apply for if you’re struggling to pay your rent.Emergency Rental Assistance ProgramThe Indiana Emergency Rental Assistance program can provide up to 12 months of rental assistance for eligible residents of Indiana. The amount and time length of the aid will depend on your household size and the region of Indiana where you live. To see if you are eligible for this program, you can fill out their Indiana emergency rental assistance application.Veterans Affairs Supportive HousingIf you or someone in your household is a VA health care eligible veteran, you may be eligible for the Veterans Affairs Supportive Housing (VASH) program. This program is meant to help reduce homelessness among veterans and encourage veterans to get the healthcare treatment and assistance they need to live healthy lives in the community.Tenant-Based Rental AssistanceThe Indiana Tenant-Based Rental Assistance (TBRA) program is meant to help low-income families with at least one household member who was formerly incarcerated. The exact amount of assistance varies by household and is determined based on the following:Household income.The landlord requested rent.A rent reasonableness standard.The Salvation ArmyWhether you’ve used one of their food banks or shopped at one of their thrift stores, chances are, you’ve heard of the Salvation Army before. They offer help with a variety of housing expenses, including both rent and utilities. You can provide your zip code to locate your nearest Salvation Army location and contact them to get financial assistance.Temporary Assistance for Needy FamiliesThis is a cash assistance program that is available to households that include children under the age of 18. The exact amount given to each household is determined based on available income, such as wages and child support, compared to the need standard for a family that size. This cash assistance can help families pay rent as well as other essentials, like utilities and food.Modest Needs FoundationThe Modest Needs Foundation is focused on helping individuals and families who live just above the poverty line, making them ineligible for many common types of emergency assistance. If your household lives just above the poverty level and has recently experienced a documented emergency that left you unable to pay rent, the Modest Needs Foundation’s grants could be a helpful resource for you.Indianapolis Emergency Rental AssistanceMarion County, which includes the greater Indianapolis area, struggles with high eviction and homelessness rates. Here are some of the additional rental assistance programs available to people living in and around Indianapolis.Indianapolis Township TrusteesThe Indianapolis Township trustees provide funding to eligible Indianapolis renters in need of temporary assistance. To apply for temporary assistance, call the center and schedule an appointment. When you go in person, remember to bring proof of income, receipts for housing payments, tax returns from the previous year, some form of ID, and birth certificates for any children in the home.Direct Emergency Financial AssistanceThe Damien Center in Indianapolis offers emergency financial assistance to Indianapolis residents who need help making rent, paying for utilities, or managing other financial emergencies. Their Direct Emergency Financial Assistance (DEFA) program is a great option if you need short-term assistance.&nbsp;&nbsp;Finding Emergency Rental Assistance in IndianaWhether this is your first time learning about emergency rental assistance or you’ve been struggling for a while, there is help out there.&nbsp;For help finding the right Indiana emergency rental assistance program for your needs, you can search the Affordable Housing Hub database to get an overview of your options.Frequently Asked Questions&nbsp;What if I need housing assistance for a longer period of time?For longer-term housing assistance visit the Affordable Housing Hub to explore options in finding affordable housing. The Indiana Housing and Community Development Authority has more information on long-term housing.How long does it take to receive rent assistance?Depending on the type of program you are applying for, receiving aid can take. It is also never guaranteed that you will receive emergency rent assistance as funding is almost always limited, so it is important to start the process as soon as possible.&nbsp;&nbsp;Is IERA available in every county of Indiana?No, each county varies in the type of assistance available and some are not participating in IERA. Marion County and Hamilton County in particular run separate housing assistance programs, so you will need to go through the county to apply to those programs.&nbsp;
