### Iowa Emergency Rental Assistance: 2025 Application Guide
Iowa was among the states with the highest average rent increase in the country in 2023. With the cost of housing going up and wages remaining stagnant, even the most cautious of renters can find themselves in an emergency situation where they are unable to make rent. Fortunately, there are programs and community organizations across Iowa working hard to help families stay in their homes.&nbsp;Eligibility for Emergency Rental Assistance Programs in IowaThough each program’s requirements may vary somewhat, you are likely eligible for some sort of rent assistance in Iowa if one or more of the following applies to you:Your income is at or below 80% of the median for your area.&nbsp;You recently became unemployed and will temporarily not have enough money to make rent.You can demonstrate significant financial hardship due to some other emergency situation.Renters who are particularly vulnerable, such as the elderly or those with children, are generally prioritized for emergency rent assistance.Statewide Rental Assistance ProgramsHere’s some information about each of the statewide emergency rental assistance programs available to Iowa residents.Emergency Rental Assistance ProgramSeveral Iowa counties participate in the Emergency Rental Assistance Program, which is a nationwide program to help those struggling to make rent. The state of Iowa works with IMPACT, a community action organization, in order to process applications and distribute aid to Iowa renters who need it. At this time, this program is only able to provide one month of rent assistance at a time. For longer-term assistance, your family may be assigned to a caseworker to help navigate other housing options. IMPACT also provides other essential services including food and utility assistance, which may help your family to sustain enough financial resources to make rent overall.&nbsp;Home and Community Based Rent Subsidy ProgramThe Iowa Finance Authority coordinates the Home and Community Based Rent Subsidy program, which provides monthly rent assistance for a limited period of time. Those receiving any other form of rent assistance are not eligible for this program. If you do not qualify for other rental assistance programs, this may be a good option for you.Central Iowa Community ServicesCentral Iowa Community Services (CICS) is a charity organization specifically designed for those with Behavioral Health Issues and intellectual disabilities. CICS provides several resources and services including emergency financial support across 15 Iowa counties.&nbsp;Iowa Veterans Trust FundIf you or someone else in your household is a veteran, you may be eligible to receive financial assistance from the Iowa Veterans Trust Fund. This program offers support for a variety of expenses, including rent. To qualify, you must be a veteran and your household must earn 300% of the federal poverty line or lower based on household size.Family Investment ProgramThis is Iowa’s version of Temporary Assistance to Needy Families (TANF). This program is available to households with children under the age of 18, whether it’s a one- or two-parent family or other relatives caring for children without parents in the home. You can receive payments for up to five years, after which you will need a hardship exemption to continue receiving payments.County Rental Assistance ProgramsMost rental assistance programs in Iowa are focused on a specific county or area. This allows organizations to provide location-specific assistance and account for the unique needs of their communities. Here are some examples of valuable county-specific emergency rental assistance programs in Iowa.Des MoinesIn the Des Moines area, CROSS Outreach is a small nonprofit that may be able to provide temporary rent assistance. Because it is a private organization that relies on donations, aid is not guaranteed and is given based on need and availability.&nbsp;PoweshiekIn Poweshiek County, there is aid available for families who are not already receiving assistance through subsidized housing. The county provides aid of up to $200 per month for families with no children and up to $325 per month for families with children.&nbsp;JohnsonThe Johnson County General Assistance program has financial assistance available for needy families in the region. This short-term financial aid can go toward rent or other essentials like utilities, prescriptions, or transportation.LinnIn Linn County, St Vincent de Paul Cedar Rapids can provide rent and utility assistance for those who bring in a physical copy of their signed lease. This type of assistance is available up to one time every six months for renters in need.&nbsp;Other CountiesIn general, most social assistance in Iowa is small-scale. There are countless grassroots organizations within Iowa that help to provide whatever aid they can to those who need it. If you don’t see your county listed above, you can search the Affordable Housing Hub to find emergency rental assistance programs near you.For further information and to explore potential options for emergency rental assistance, contact us at contact@affordablehousinghub.org&nbsp;

### Kansas Emergency Rental Assistance: 2025 Application Guide
During times of financial hardship, many families and individuals across the country need help making their rental payments. If you are currently living in Kansas, you might already be aware that the Kansas Emergency Rental Assistance program has closed. However, there are still other ways you can access the support and resources you need. Let’s go over some of the main rental assistance programs available to Kansas residents in 2025.Kansas Emergency Rental Assistance (KERA)The Kansas Emergency Rental Assistance (KERA) program, run by the Kansas Housing Resources Corporation, started in March 2021 and ended in February 2023. At the time of its closure, sufficient funding was no longer available to continue offering assistance to every household that applied.Throughout its 1.5 year duration, the program provided more than $290 million in relief for over 82,000 Kansas residents. It also prevented evictions in an estimated 32,000 households across the state.Tenant Based Rental Assistance (TBRA)The Tenant Based Rental Assistance (TBRA) program is another program offered by the Kansas Housing Resources Corporation that is still active. Through TBRA, income-eligible households can access financial resources to help pay for rent, security deposits, and utility deposits.Different agencies provide funding for various locations across the state. You can submit your application to a corresponding agency depending on the county or city in which you currently live. You can find a full list of agencies and the counties or cities they serve as well as any documents and forms necessary for the application process on the TBRA home page.Kansas CityIf you’re looking for an emergency rental assistance program in Kansas City, there is no shortage of supportive organizations. The Kansas City, Kansas (KCK) Housing Authority lists many of them along with their phone numbers on their website:Mount Carmel Community Outreach (913-621-4111): Rental assistance.Catholic Charities Of Wyandotte County (913- 621-3445): Rent and utility assistance.Village Presbyterian Church (913- 262-4200): Utility assistance.Metro Lutheran Ministries (913-341-8333): Rent, utility, and food assistance.USD 500 (913-551-3200): Rent and utility assistance for student families.Wyandot Center, Kim Wilson Housing (913-328-4600): Rental and mental health assistance.The KCK Housing Authority also offers public housing with rental rates that adjust based on your current income. So, if your income goes down, your rent will as well. Some residents may be able to qualify for a flat rental rate instead.Johnson CountyLow-income households in Johnson County may qualify to receive limited rental assistance. To be eligible for support, you must:Be a Johnson County resident.Provide proof that your household is at or below 200% of the federal poverty guidelines.Provide photo IDs for members of the household who are 18 or older.Provide Social Security cards for all members of the household.Provide a past-due notice or an eviction notice from the landlord.In this case, rental assistance does not apply to rental deposits. Those who are currently in a subsidized housing program cannot apply for support through this program either.Additional Kansas Housing ResourcesOften, one hardship can lead to another, leaving families unsure about how to move forward. If your household needs additional assistance with more than rent or utility payments, here is a list of various types of resources available to Kansas residents.211 of Kansas211 of Kansas is a statewide service offered through United Way that connects Kansas residents with specialized support. No matter where you live in the state, you can dial 211 to reach a specialist who will help you find the resources you need.In addition to housing support, 211 of Kansas provides resources for:Health and dental care.Mental health and addiction.Transportation.Employment and education.Legal and money management.Seniors and disability.You can also find information by visiting the 211 online directory and selecting your zip code, city, or county.Kansas Association of Community Action Programs (KACAP)The Kansas Association of Community Action Programs (KACAP) aims to help low-income households across the state find support throughout many different kinds of hardships. They provide connections to local programs that offer rental or utility assistance along with job search support, access to food pantries, and much more.To connect with resources in your area, visit the KACAP network page and click on your county.Find the Support You NeedNo household should have to face hardships alone. If you and your loved ones need access to Kansas emergency rental assistance programs or support from anywhere else in the country, Affordable Housing Hub offers a comprehensive overview of both federal and state programs that can help you find the resources you need.

### Kentucky Emergency Rental Assistance: 2025 Application Guide
Many Americans today struggle to make ends meet, especially with rising inflation in the current economy. Housing can be a large burden on those living on low income, or who are homeless or have special needs. The state of Kentucky provides a number of different options available for residents looking for emergency housing, including shelters, homeowner funds, assistance programs, and Section 8 housing. Below is a comprehensive guide to finding emergency rental assistance for Kentucky residents.Assistance ProgramsThese programs are available to Kentuckians through the government and allow for help with bills and other home services. These include, but are not limited to:The Team Kentucky Healthy at Home Eviction Relief Fund can help renters with overdue utility bills up to 15 months past due. Renters and landlords can apply for rental assistance online and view the list of requirements to see if they are eligible.The Homeowner Assistance Fund exists to help homeowners with eviction notices, utility services, and foreclosures. It was created in 2020 during COVID-19 to help those affected by the pandemic, allowing qualified candidates to apply for up to $35,000 in assistance.&nbsp;VouchersVouchers can be used to provide rental assistance for low-income individuals and families struggling with finding housing. Some vouchers available include:VETT Vouchers: these vouchers are available for veterans in select counties impacted by homelessness.Housing Choice Voucher (HCV) RENTCafé: this website contains online housing services available to tenants and landlords.Emergency Housing Vouchers: these vouchers are available to homeless families who meet specific criteria.Section 8 HousingSection 8 Housing is funded by the U.S. Department of Housing and Urban Development (HUD) and seeks to provide rental assistance to low-income families and individuals. In the state of Kentucky, the program is run by the Kentucky Housing Corporation (KHC), and applicants must meet certain criteria to be eligible for assistance, including:A household income at or below 50% of the median incomePassing a criminal background check since specific crimes would disqualify individuals from assistance&nbsp;A good rental history with no previous outstanding debtsNumber of people in the householdAgeDisabilityMust be a U.S. citizen, U.S. national, or a non-citizen with eligible immigration statusSection 8 will pay a maximum amount of 30% of a household’s total income, but this number can vary based on several factors including the number of bedrooms and the location of the rental unit.&nbsp;Application ProcessInterested candidates can begin the application process by finding an open waiting list on the KHC website or by getting in touch with local representatives. Once they find an open list, they can continue the process which includes the following steps:Complete the Section 8 application through the website or on paper through KHCProvide necessary documentation including, but not limited to, proof of income, citizenship, and rental historyComplete an interview with KHC or local housing authority to further determine eligibility.&nbsp;See if you have been approved for Section 8 housing assistance and added to the waitlist&nbsp;The Kentucky Housing Authorities are a helpful resource available throughout the application process. There are several branches throughout Kentucky so applicants can contact the closest one in their specific area for more information. They also manage the wait list for Section 8 Housing which can last for years due to high demand.SheltersThere are several shelters in place for those affected by homelessness in Kentucky.&nbsp;For those in Lexington-Fayette County, you can contact the Office of Homelessness Prevention and Intervention.For Louisville and Jefferson County residents, the Coalition for the Homeless will provide good resources for assistance.For all other areas of Kentucky, you can contact the Kentucky Housing Corporation or find resources on their website.Additional Housing ResourcesIf you require further options for rental assistance, there are additional resources available in Kentucky such as:Public Housing: This resource is run by local housing authorities and can include units with immediate availabilityPrivate Rental Markets: Some landlords will offer affordable units to low-income families and individuals through rent subsidies or with units located in housing developments&nbsp;Low-Income Housing Tax Credit Properties: These are units funded by federal tax credits for low-income householdsRural Development Housing: This program is run by the U.S. Department of Agriculture (USDA) and includes resources such as rental assistance, grants, and home loansThere is a wide range of resources available to Kentuckians struggling with financial hardships and homelessness. Though the homelessness crisis is growing and waitlists might seem endless, it is still important to utilize the resources available if you seek financial assistance.

### Louisiana Emergency Rental Assistance: 2025 Application Guide
Many Louisiana residents today struggle to make ends meet, especially with rising inflation in the current economy. Housing can be a large burden on those living on a low income. Fortunately, there are several Louisiana emergency rental assistance programs that can help you find and maintain stable housing.Here’s how to get help paying rent and other essential bills for your Louisiana home.Emergency Rental Assistance Programs in LouisianaHere are some popular government-funded emergency rental assistance programs available across the state.Tenant-Based Rental Assistance (TBRA)The TBRA program is an emergency rental assistance program available through the Louisiana Housing Corporation. This program addresses the needs of individuals and families in need throughout the state. Depending on your eligibility, TBRA can help you with money for rent payments, security deposits, utility payments, and utility deposits.&nbsp;Section 8 HousingSection 8 Housing in Louisiana is a federal program run by the Louisiana Housing Corporation. The program seeks to provide rental assistance to low-income families and individuals who are in need of safe and affordable housing.&nbsp;In order to qualify for housing, applicants must meet certain criteria, which include:A household income at or below 50% of the median incomeNumber of people in the householdInterested candidates can begin the application process by finding their local housing authority either online or through your local HUD office. Once the application is submitted, it can take up to a few months to get approved depending on the volume of applicants.Multifamily Housing Rental AssistanceIf you live in a USDA-financed Rural Rental Housing or Farm Labor Housing building, you may be eligible to receive financial assistance from the USDA. This program makes payments on the tenants’ behalf to owners of eligible projects that are run on a non-profit or limited-profit basis. If you think you may qualify, consider discussing this type of rental assistance with your landlord.Additional Emergency Rental Assistance Resources in LouisianaIf you require further options for housing assistance, there are additional resources available in Louisiana. Some help with rent or other important housing expenses, such as utility bills.Louisiana Low-Income Home Energy Assistance ProgramIf you’re experiencing housing insecurity because you are not able to pay your utility bills, the Low-Income Home Energy Assistance Program (LIHEAP) may be able to help you. LIHEAP offers financial assistance to families that need help paying their energy bills and prioritizes households with members who are children, elderly, or disabled.To qualify for this program, your household must earn less than 60% of the state median household income. If you receive other benefits, such as SNAP, SSI, or TANF, you automatically meet this eligibility requirement.Catholic Charities of North LouisianaThis program offers both short-term financial assistance with rent and utility bills and long-term help through financial education resources. Depending on your parish, the Catholic Charities of North Louisiana may be able to help you with emergency assistance once per year or once every two years.Catholic Charities of South LouisianaMuch like the Catholic Charities of North Louisiana, the Catholic Charities of South Louisiana organization can help you with financial assistance for rent and other essential bills. They currently offer help to eligible people living in Allen, Beauregard, Calcasieu, Cameron, and Jefferson Davis parishes. You can call them to set up an appointment to applyWhen you apply, you’ll need to bring several documents showing your circumstances, including but not limited to a photo ID, proof of income for everyone in the household, and your current lease.Volunteers of America South Central LouisianaThis organization provides housing support and other resources for people with a diagnosis of HIV/AIDS in these parishes:AscensionEast and West Baton RougeEast and West FelicianaIbervilleLivingstonPointe CoupeeYou may be eligible to receive support services such as emergency financial assistance for housing and utility bills. You can also apply for help with other essentials such as food and transportation.Louisiana Department of Veterans AffairsIf you or someone else in your household is a veteran, you may qualify for rental assistance from the Louisiana Department of Veterans Affairs. They offer a variety of programs to help veterans who are facing homelessness. You can get personalized help for your situation by getting in touch with your local Parish Service Office.Protecting Your Louisiana HomeIf you call a place in Louisiana home, we want to help you keep it that way. There are several rental assistance programs, vouchers, and online resources readily available to give low-income residents the opportunity to find and maintain stable housing.&nbsp;To see what rental assistance programs are available in your area, try out the Affordable Housing Hub’s search tool. You can simply put in your zip code and get a thorough list of programs that may be able to help your household make rent each month.

### Maine Emergency Rental Assistance: 2025 Application Guide
In recent decades, housing instability has been a pressing issue, especially during the past couple of years. Due to economic disruptions, many Maine residents are struggling to cover housing costs.&nbsp; Though the leading emergency rental assistance program in Maine is no longer accepting applications, several other options are available for those in need.&nbsp;If you're one of many searching for an emergency rental assistance program in your state, take a moment to explore these resources.Do You Need an Emergency Rental Assistance Program in Maine?Emergency rental assistance (ERA) programs aim to help Maine tenants who struggle to pay rent due to unforeseen hardships. This may include job loss, reduced work hours, medical conditions, and other challenges. ERA programs provide qualified individuals and families with funds to cover rent, utilities, and other housing-related costs.&nbsp;Each program has its own list of requirements and services the organization provides. So, if you're in need of housing assistance, research your state's programs carefully. This way, you'll be more likely to apply for and access the right services.&nbsp;Let's explore a few local programs that cover emergency rental assistance.Maine Community Action PartnershipThe Maine Community Action Partnership (MeCAP) helps empower low-income individuals and families by providing a range of housing services. This organization works with several other Community Action Agencies across the state to offer qualified residents housing assistance, energy assistance, and other housing-related programs that keep residents housed in safe environments.MaineHousing SubsidiesMaineHousing is an organization that provides an array of subsidy programs that make housing more affordable for low-income residents. These programs can cover rent costs, some utilities, and other needs that residents experience. MaineHousing may also assist in home repair and weatherization needs so that they can ensure safe living conditions for families.Housing Choice Voucher ProgramThe Housing Choice Voucher program, or Section 8, is a federal program that's controlled by local public housing authorities. This program provides low-income families, seniors, and individuals with disabilities with housing assistance.&nbsp;Section 8 housing vouchers make it easier for Maine residents to afford decent and safe housing throughout the state. Participants pay a portion of their income toward rent, with the voucher covering the remainder.Maine Emergency SheltersMaine Emergency Shelters isn't necessarily an emergency rental assistance program in Maine. However, this program does offer temporary housing and supportive services to individuals and families facing homelessness. These shelters offer residents a safe place to stay, along with access to food, case management, and resources designed to help simplify the transition into stable housing.211 MaineFor individuals who are struggling to find the right program for their needs, 211 Maine can help. This information and referral service is both free and confidential, and it works to connect people to local resources.&nbsp;A couple of these resources include housing assistance, food programs, and healthcare-related services. Maine residents can call 2-1-1 or visit the 211 Maine website to get help finding the support they need any time of day.HUD’s Permanent Supported Housing ProgramThe U.S. Department of Housing and Urban Development (HUD) provides Permanent Supported Housing (PSH) programs in Maine. These programs help individuals who are homeless or at risk, especially those living with disabilities.&nbsp;Through PSH programs, Maine residents can secure long-term housing as well as various supportive services. For example, PSH programs may cover mental health counseling, substance abuse treatment, and job training. These services help ensure that individuals can maintain their housing.Bridging Rental Assistance ProgramThe Bridging Rental Assistance Program (BRAP) offers temporary rental assistance to individuals who live with psychiatric conditions and are either homeless or at risk. BRAP helps cover the cost of a resident's housing costs until these individuals can secure more permanent rent subsidies. In addition to rental assistance, BRAP offers supportive services that enable housing stability.Finding the Right Emergency Rental Assistance Program in MaineDespite the fact that several local programs exist, it can be challenging to find the right one for your family’s needs. If you’re struggling to find an emergency rental assistance program in Maine, contact or visit your local Department of Health and Human Services (DHHS) office. A caseworker should be able to provide you with a list of resources to explore.&nbsp;An emergency rental assistance program in Maine can make a world of difference for those experiencing housing instability. By being familiar with the available programs, individual eligibility requirements, and the application process, you can take steps toward securing housing assistance. Take time to explore your options, ask questions, and collaborate with experienced caseworkers for the best outcome.For more on state programs, explore the resources available at the Affordable Housing Hub. Take a look at open waiting lists and more to find affordable housing.

### Maryland Emergency Rental Assistance: 2025 Application Guide
There’s no denying that rent has become a burdensome expense for many families in Maryland. Emergency rental assistance programs therefore play a crucial role in helping Maryland residents who are experiencing financial setbacks stay housed.&nbsp;Without these vital programs, many families could face the harsh reality of eviction and homelessness. If you are looking for emergency rental assistance in MD, here is a guide to help you understand the Emergency Rental Assistance Program in Maryland as well as other resources that are available to you.211 Maryland Referral Specialists211 Maryland is a one-stop resource for individuals and families seeking help with finding or maintaining affordable housing. This service is particularly valuable for those who are unsure where to start when it comes to seeking financial assistance. If you’re facing eviction or need help paying rent, you can dial 211 to speak with a 211 Maryland referral specialist who will connect you with resources. These specialists are trained to listen to your situation and provide tailored advice and support, ensuring you get the help you need as quickly as possible.211 Maryland SearchIn addition to offering phone consultations, 211 Maryland also has an online search tool that you can use to find rental payment assistance programs throughout Maryland. This user-friendly tool allows you to search for resources based on your specific location and needs, making it easier to find the right assistance. Whether you need immediate help or are planning for the future, the online search tool is a valuable resource. The website also offers additional information on other forms of assistance, such as food aid and healthcare resources, making it a comprehensive support system for Maryland residents.Emergency Assistance to Families with Children (EAFC)The EAFC Program provides cash assistance to families with children who need emergency help paying rent or utilities. This program is designed to offer a safety net for families who are experiencing a temporary financial crisis. Maryland residents can apply for EAFC assistance at their local Department of Human Services office as well as online. To streamline the application process, it’s important to carefully review the eligibility criteria and required application items before applying.&nbsp;Emergency Rental Assistance ProgramMaryland residents can receive Emergency Rental Assistance Program funds through their local government. These funds are designed to help residents who are unable to pay their rent due to unforeseen circumstances such as job loss, medical emergencies, or other financial hardships.&nbsp;The Emergency Rental Assistance Program sends federal funding to location jurisdictions in Maryland. The local jurisdictions utilize the funding to help Marylanders experiencing financial setbacks maintain their housing.&nbsp;Maryland agencies are required to prioritize Emergency Rental Assistance Program funding for the following household types:Households with an annual income at or below 50% of the Area Median Income (AMI), which is determined by the U.S. Department of Housing and Urban Development (HUD).Households with one or more individuals who are unemployed at the time of application and who have not been employed for the last 90 days.Visit the Emergency Rental Assistance Program page of the Maryland Department of Housing and Community Development website to see information on where to apply for assistance in your county. You can use this webpage’s information to get in touch with the appropriate agency in your county. Your local agency will then be able to provide you with more detailed information on eligibility requirements, documentation, and deadlines.&nbsp;Maryland Emergency Rental Assistance ResourcesResidents of Maryland who are struggling to pay rent can receive various forms of assistance from state and local agencies, as well as non-profit organizations. These resources are essential for preventing homelessness and ensuring that families remain safe and stable.&nbsp;Maryland emergency rental assistance is a lifeline for many families facing financial hardship. By utilizing services like 211 Maryland, the EAFC Program, and the Emergency Rental Assistance Program, residents can find the help they need to stay in their homes.Remember to seek help as soon as you anticipate difficulties with paying rent, as early intervention can prevent eviction and other serious consequences. The resources and programs available are designed to provide support and stability during tough times, ensuring that Maryland residents have the opportunity to thrive despite financial challenges.It is also important to remember that each assistance program has its own deadlines, application requirements, and eligibility criteria. Proactively researching Maryland emergency rental assistance resources and contacting appropriate agencies can be a great way to ensure you receive the help you need.&nbsp;For more information on emergency rental assistance in MD, visit the Maryland Department of Housing and Community Development. This website contains updates on emergency rental assistance programs, overviews of different agencies and organizations that support renters who are experiencing financial hardships, and housing education resources for Maryland renters. You can also consult the numerous rental assistance resources mentioned in this Affordable Housing Hub guide.&nbsp;

### Massachusetts Emergency Rental Assistance: 2025 Application Guide
More and more people are in need of emergency rental assistance. Massachusetts is no exception; as of 2023, emergency rental assistance programs made nearly 10 million payments to families at risk of eviction. Lucky for Bay Staters in financial crises, a couple options are available to you so you can stay located in your current home or relocate to a new one.Finding Emergency Rental Assistance, MAHaving one of the highest costs of living in the country, it is no wonder that some are beginning to rely on an emergency rental assistance program in Massachusetts known as RAFT, or Residential Assistance for Families in Transition. RAFT can provide funds of up to $7,000 per year to families, which can allow them to relocate or afford their current home. This money can be used for a variety of purposes including rent, utilities, and moving expenses. The RAFT application takes between 20 and 30 minutes to complete.Another resource for Bay Staters is housing vouchers, which can be provided on a state or federal level. At the state level, the emergency rental assistance program in Massachusetts is called CHAMP, or Common Housing Application for Massachusetts Programs. On the CHAMP site, you will be able to apply for state-aided subsidized housing. Similarly, the Metro North Regional Housing Services Office,&nbsp; MNRHSO, has its own emergency rental assistance program that can pay up to 18 months of rent.Also at the state level, you may be able to apply for the Massachusetts Rental Voucher Program, or MRVP, which offers rental vouchers to low-income families. Vouchers can be either tenant-based or project-based, so you can decide what works best for you and your current situation.At the federal level, you can apply for the HCVP ( Section 8 Housing Choice Vouchers Program). If accepted into the program, you will receive vouchers that you can pay towards your rent while being required to pay only 30% of your rent out of pocket. Currently, no online application is available, so to apply for this program, you will have to go in person to a Regional Administrating Agency.&nbsp;If You Can’t Find an Emergency Rental Assistance Program in Massachusetts That Works for YouUnfortunately, due to limited resources, not everyone qualifies for emergency assistance. Thankfully, Bay Staters do have a couple of other options available to them when in a tight spot. The Commonwealth of Massachusetts offers emergency housing assistance to those in need of immediate shelter. While shelters are only temporary, they can serve as transitional housing while you are in between jobs or in a housing crisis. There are specific resources available to youths, adults, and those who are pregnant or have children under the age of 21.Additionally, the Housing Toolbox for Massachusetts Communities directly addresses the limited resources offered by the state, so please visit their website for more information regarding what assistance may be available to you and your family.Typically, each community has churches and local charities they can rely on in times of crisis. For example, Catholic churches and the Salvation Army are usually able to assist in paying rent for those who need it.&nbsp;For those uninterested in supporting religious organizations, other options for charities are available such as United Way and Habitat for Humanity.&nbsp;Next Steps in Finding HousingThis may be a difficult time for you, but we just want to remind you that you are not alone - an insurmountable number of people are in the same boat as you, which is why we are here to refer you to the resources available and emergency rental assistance. Massachusetts has one of the highest costs of living in the country, but we don’t blame you for wanting to stay; whether it’s for the immaculate summer days, the fascinating history, or the world-famous seafood, Massachusetts is your home for a reason.Being in financial hardship can be quite overwhelming, but we want you to know that we are here to help. If you have questions or need assistance, please contact us, and we would be happy to walk you through your resources and next steps.&nbsp;

The program provides vouchers that cover a portion of rent based on family size and income. With housing vouchers, families are free to choose single family homes, apartments, condos, and other options.&nbsp;Eligibility Requirements:Income at or below 50% of the local median incomeU.S. citizenship or eligible immigration statusBackground checksTemporary Cash AssistanceTemporary Cash Assistance is available to Michigan residents who are pregnant or have minor children and meet income requirements. The program also helps families with minor children access, job skill training, child care, transportation to work and more. Michigan residents may receive a lifetime total of 60 cash payments to help with rent, utilities, groceries, and more.&nbsp;Eligibility Requirements:Must have a minor child at home or a child over 18 who is currently enrolled in high schoolIncome requirements are based on ages and number of childrenOpen to Michigan residentsWhy Emergency Rental Assistance MattersPrograms that help Michigan residents and families stay in their homes have a deep and lasting impact on communities. ### Minnesota Emergency Rental Assistance: 2025 Application Guide
Some programs offering emergency rental assistance have ended since the height of the COVID-19 pandemic. There are still several Minnesota emergency rental assistance programs available to help residents facing housing insecurity. It can be challenging to face losing your home but there are state and local programs here to help. Learn more about the programs available to you and how they impact the communities they serve.Minnesota State Emergency Rental Assistance ProgramsHere are some popular programs that are available across the state of Minnesota.RentHelpMN Targeted AssistanceThe Minnesota Housing Finance Agency administers the RentHelpMN Targeted Assistance program, which offers residents impacted by the COVID-19 pandemic. This referral-based program is federally funded and aims to provide housing stability. Program administrators identify eligible renters and walk them through the application process.Here are the main qualifying criteria for this program:At or below 80% of the local median income.At risk of housing insecurity.Suffered financial hardship or unemployment during the pandemic.Minnesota Housing Trust Fund Rental Assistance ProgramThe Minnesota Housing Trust Fund Rental Assistance Program provides qualified occupants of income-restricted properties with rent and utility payments. To qualify for this program, residents must have suffered financial hardship due to the COVID-19 crisis. Payments are made directly to landlords and property owners on behalf of program participants.Here are the main qualifying criteria for this program:At or below 80% of the local median income.Must have experienced a loss of household income due to COVID-19.Must not currently receive full rental assistance.Lutheran Social Service of Minnesota (LSS) Rental AssistanceThe Lutheran Social Service of Minnesota Rental Assistance program provides households with back rent payments and future rent payments. Payments are made directly to property owners on behalf of program recipients.Here are the main qualifying criteria for this program:At or below 80% of the local median income.Must have experienced a loss of household income due to COVID-19.Hennepin County Emergency Rental AssistanceHennepin County offers emergency assistance for qualifying residents facing financial hardship and housing insecurity. Residents can use program funds to pay rent and utilities. Several nonprofits and service organizations collaborate under this program. Residents may qualify for multiple services with one application under this program.Here are the main qualifying criteria for this program:At or below 80% of the local median income.Must have experienced a loss of household income due to COVID-19.Must reside in Hennepin County.Emergency Rental Assistance in Ramsey County, MNRamsey County offers its residents emergency rental assistance to cope with the effects of the COVID-19 pandemic. This program prioritizes individuals and families facing imminent eviction and housing insecurity.Here are the main qualifying criteria for this program:At or below 80% of the local median income.Must have experienced a loss of household income due to COVID-19.Must reside in Ramsey County.East Central Minnesota Emergency Housing AssistanceThe East Central Minnesota Emergency Housing Assistance program offers qualified residents funds for rent, mortgage, and utility payments. This program aims to keep Minnesota residents in their homes by avoiding eviction.&nbsp;Here are the main qualifying criteria for this program:Proof of qualifying income for all adults.Documentation of rental agreement.Documentation of overdue payments and housing insecurities.Itasca and Koochiching Counties Crisis Rent Assistance ProgramApplicants to the Itasca and Kooching Counties Crisis Rent Assistance program must go through a phone or in-person screening to determine if they qualify for assistance. This program is aimed at preventing evictions and keeping people in their homes. Residents must provide the following documentation to be considered:Verification of the last 30 days of household income.Third-party verification of homelessness (if relevant).Notice of eviction (if relevant).Documentation of crisis.Documentation of any funds paid toward managing the crisis.Scott and Carver Counties Energy AssistanceThe Scott and Carver Counties Energy Assistance program helps qualified residents pay for rent, utility bills, and heating costs. Program funds can apply to utility disconnections and fuel delivery as well. This program is focused on providing vulnerable families access to essential services. Income requirements for this program vary based on the size of your household.How Rental Support Benefits Minnesota CommunitiesWhen long-term residents lose their housing to eviction, Minnesota communities suffer. Keeping residents in their homes often means keeping them in their jobs and schools. Poverty and housing insecurity weaken our communities. That’s why rental assistance programs are so important. ### Missouri Emergency Rental Assistance: 2025 Application Guide
Housing insecurity is urgent and overwhelming but there are resources to provide relief. Find out how emergency rental assistance programs in Missouri can help you avoid losing your home.&nbsp;Statewide Missouri Emergency Rental AssistanceHere are a few programs that are available to Missouri residents across the state.Missouri State Assistance for Housing Relief ProgramThe Missouri State Assistance for Housing Relief (SAFHR) program provides help to both landlords and tenants impacted by the COVID-19 pandemic. This program covers past due, current, and up to three months of future rent and utility bill payments. Under the SAFHR program landlords receive timely payments and renters have housing security.&nbsp;To be eligible for this program, you must:Earn 80% or less of the local median income.Demonstrate financial hardship due to the COVID-19 pandemic.Be at risk of homelessness or housing insecurity.Missouri Emergency Rental Arrears ProgramEligible landlords in Missouri can get support for tenants’ past due rental payments dating back to April 2020 through the Emergency Rental Arrears Program. This program requires collaboration between tenants and landlords. Landlords apply on behalf of tenants and must agree not to evict tenants within 120 days of receiving funding. This keeps more Missouri residents in their homes and protects landlords from having to file evictions and raise rental prices.You may be eligible for this program if your landlord is willing to apply cooperatively with you and your past due rent is because of the COVID-19 pandemic.Local Emergency Rental Assistance ProgramsMany counties and cities within Missouri offer emergency rental assistance programs of their own. They may also be able to offer more location-specific assistance and income requirements. Here are a few popular local emergency rental assistance programs you may want to consider.Kansas City Emergency Rental Assistance ProgramAs part of a wider initiative by Kansas City to prevent evictions and curb homelessness, the Kansas City Emergency Rental Assistance Program provides funding for past-due rent and future rent payments to stabilize housing for residents. This program is funded through the CARES Act and is aimed at preventing homelessness in vulnerable communities.&nbsp;To be eligible for this program, you must:Earn 80% or less of the local median income.&nbsp;Demonstrate financial hardship due to the COVID-19 pandemic.Live in St. Louis County.Greene County Emergency Rental Assistance ProgramApplicants to the Greene County Emergency Rental Assistance Program must be screened in person, by appointment. A local community agency walks eligible residents through the application process step by step. This local program offers emergency rental assistance in Springfield MO and other Greene County population centers.At the time of application, the following documents are required:A list of household members.Identification for all household members.Income information for all adults in the household.Proof of unemployment or lost wages due to COVID-19.Copies of past-due rent and utility bills.A copy of your lease or rental agreement.Landlord/property owner’s contact information.Kansas City Reconciliation Services Emergency Rental AssistanceReconciliation Services offers qualified Kansas City residents emergency rental assistance to cope with the effects of the COVID-19 pandemic. Program funds can be used to cover overdue rent and utility bills so residents can avoid eviction.&nbsp;To be eligible for this program, you must:Earn 80% or less of the local median income.&nbsp;Demonstrate financial hardship due to the COVID-19 pandemic.Live in Kansas City.The Effect of Rental Assistance on Missouri CommunitiesCommunities across Missouri feel a significant impact from rental assistance programs that keep long-term residents in their homes. ### Montana Emergency Rental Assistance: 2025 Application Guide
Many COVID-era rental relief programs have ended but there are still multiple Montana emergency rental assistance programs that can help residents stay in their homes. The threat of housing insecurity can feel overpowering, but there are programs to help. Find out how to apply for emergency rental assistance in Montana and how these programs benefit communities.&nbsp;Montana Emergency Rental Assistance ProgramThe Montana Emergency Rental Assistance (MERA) program provides residents experiencing housing instability with financial support. Eligible households could receive up to $2,200 for rent, $300 for utilities, and $50 for internet service each month. However, the amount each household receives is calculated based on their income and expenses.To qualify, households must be able to prove significant financial hardship related to the financial impacts of the COVID-19 pandemic, earn 80% or less of the local median household income, and demonstrate the threat of housing instability.Montana Housing Choice Voucher ProgramMontant residents with disabilities, low-income families, and senior citizens can access safe and affordable housing through the Montana Housing Choice Voucher Program through the Department of Commerce. Qualified households can choose their preferred housing in the community. Recipients pay approximately 30% of their gross adjusted income toward rent. The subsidy covers the rest.&nbsp;The amount of the subsidy may be adjusted as the household’s income changes, so it’s important to update your information regularly as jobs change, whether your income is going up or down. You may qualify for this program if you meet HUD income guidelines. Applications are divided into regions, so make sure you’re submitting the right application for your county.&nbsp;Veterans Affairs Supportive Housing ProgramThe Veterans Affairs Supportive Housing (HUD-VASH) Program offers qualifying homeless veterans in Montana case management and clinical services. Through this program, Montana residents who are veterans or have veterans in their households can receive vouchers to help them secure and maintain housing.&nbsp;Eligibility screenings are conducted by the US Department of Veteran Affairs case management team. To qualify for this program, you must:Receive ongoing case management.Have prior military service.&nbsp;Meet income requirements.Project-Based Section 8The project-based Section 8 Program in Montana works by funding apartments, not individual occupants. Typically, residents will only be expected to pay about 30% of their household income as rent. A Housing Assistance Payment contract covers the rest, adjusting with the household’s income over time. This program is administered by Montana Housing at the Montana Department of Commerce.&nbsp;Section 811 Supportive Housing for Persons with DisabilitiesThis critical program supports Montant residents with disabilities and promotes their independence wherever possible. HUD supplies funding to subsidize and develop housing that specifically serves low-income adults with disabilities. It can provide interest-free capital advances for the development of accessible housing for the disabled.&nbsp;These capital advances do not need to be repaid as long as the housing is available for low-income adults with disabilities for at least 40 years, incentivizing the management to keep their pricing accessible.Disabled people and the families that care for them are especially vulnerable to housing instability. Programs like this can help ease hardships for families and allow them to focus on caring for their disabled family members. This program can also make it easier for low-income disabled adults to secure housing that is both financially and physically accessible.NeighborWorks Montana Rental AssistanceThe NeighborWorks program provides counseling to renters and housing education through a network of HUD-approved agencies. This program works with local organizations to help renters apply for federal, state, and local emergency rental assistance. If you need help stabilizing your housing situation, this organization can minimize the stress and anxiety of the application process.&nbsp;To qualify for this program, you must:Earn 80% or less of the local median incomeDemonstrate the threat of housing instability&nbsp;The Importance of Rental Assistance in Local CommunitiesHousing insecurity can have a significant impact on communities. When Montana residents and their families are removed from their homes, social ties are damaged. Individuals may experience the stress of starting over with new housing, jobs, and schools.Programs that help Montana residents facing eviction and housing insecurity play a major role in combating the negative effects of the pandemic on Montana communities. Keeping more people in their homes helps communities by encouraging strong relationships and allowing people to continue developing friendships with the people at their jobs and schools.Accessing Help with Rent in MontanaIf you need support to maintain stable housing and reduce the financial effects of the COVID-19 pandemic on your household, emergency rental assistance programs may be able to help.&nbsp;To see what emergency rental assistance programs are available in your area, consider using the Affordable Housing Hub’s tool to search and apply for emergency rental assistance programs and low-income housing options.

Falling behind on rental payments can result in stress and anxiety. However, help is available for many Nebraskans. Users can select the area in which they live and immediately view a variety of resources available to them, ranging from childcare and education assistance to senior services. If you’re unclear what services are available to you, simply select your region on their page.Emergency Rental Assistance in Douglas County, NERental assistance programs in Douglas County can be divided into two categories: those aimed towards renters within the city limits of Omaha and those meant for renters outside.Emergency rental Assistance in Omaha, NEIf you live in the city of Omaha, rental assistance is available through the Threshold Continuum of Care (CoC). This network of organizations is dedicated to preventing homelessness and supporting stable living for citizens of Omaha. As with most other financial assistance initiatives, Omaha renters must prove financial hardship in order to receive funds. To connect with Threshold CoC, you can reach out to your local access point.Rental Assistance in Douglas County outside of Omaha City LimitsFor those living in Douglas County outside the city limits of Omaha, your nearest emergency rental assistance comes through the Christian Outreach Program - Elkhorn (COPE). This system helps streamline resources related to housing and emergency , as well as the surrounding Lancaster County. For this reason, the All Leads Home System can also be used to apply for help paying for utilities. The application portal for both forms of assistance is clear and simple, and further assistance can be found using the MyLink website.Nebraska Emergency Rental Assistance Program (ERA)For those living in the more rural parts of Nebraska outside of the Omaha and Lincoln areas, the path is a bit more straightforward. If you live outside of those zones, the Nebraska Emergency Rental Assistance Program (ERA), sometimes referred to as Nebraska Rent Help, is likely your most convenient point of access to rental assistance.Authorized in 2021, this program was created with the intention of supporting those whose finances were impacted by the COVID-19 pandemic. While many states saw rollbacks in ERA programs over the course of 2023, Nebraska has continued to support struggling renters through this assistance.Applying for Nebraska Emergency Rental AssistanceIn a similar manner to the qualifications put in place in 2021, applicants must provide certain documentation in order to be granted funds. This might include:A signed and valid rental agreementProof of occupancyProof of household incomeProof that at least one earner in the household has had their income affected by COVID-19Landlords can also apply for funding through this program in order to support stable housing. Completed applications for landlords include:An IRS W-9 formA signed rental or lease agreementProof of rental arrears owedDocumentation of other subsidies, as applicableFurther Rental Assistance for NebraskansWhile the Nebraska Emergency Rental Assistance program has helped countless renters, it’s not the only form of support out there. Plenty of federal resources exist to help keep your housing stable. For more information about what federal programs may apply to you, check out our Rental Assistance Overview.

### Nevada Emergency Rental Assistance: 2025 Application Guide
Economic hardships are not uncommon for Nevada residents. Because of this, covering housing expenses can be challenging. Job losses, reduced hours, and the higher cost of living has caused the need for rental assistance to skyrocket. Due to widespread need, state organizations have worked to provide support through Nevada emergency rental assistance programs.&nbsp;If you're a Nevada tenant and you're struggling to make ends meet, it's important to get familiar with the different assistance programs available.Understanding Nevada Emergency Rental AssistanceMany individuals and families in Nevada struggle to keep up with the ever-increasing cost of rents throughout the state. In response to these challenges, several government and charitable organizations have established programs to help residents secure safe, affordable housing. Numerous programs exist, and each has its own set of eligibility requirements, application processes, rules, and waiting lists.&nbsp;Let's go over some of the unique Nevada emergency rental assistance programs that stand to help the state's citizens.Nevada CARES Act Housing AssistanceThe Nevada CARES Act Housing Assistance Program was established to provide housing assistance to Nevadans in the wake of the COVID-19 pandemic. This program offers individuals and families both rental and mortgage assistance funds.&nbsp;The CARES Act helps prevent evictions and foreclosures as residents struggle to get back on their feet after the pandemic. This way, Nevada families can remain in their homes despite financial hardship. The program is available throughout Nevada, making it viable for those seeking emergency rental assistance in Reno, NV.Nevada Rural Housing Program (NRH)The Nevada Rural Housing Program offers rural Nevadans affordable housing opportunities. The program provides several services, including rental assistance, homebuyer resources, and financing options for purchasing homes. It's designed to assist low and moderate-income families with securing stable housing.Lutheran Social Services of Nevada (LSSN)Lutheran Social Services of Nevada (LSSN) offers several supportive services to Nevada families. These options include emergency rental assistance, utility assistance, and various case management services. The LSSN aims to prevent homelessness and offer a helping hand to those in need.HopeLink of Southern NevadaHopeLink of Southern Nevada has several services that assist families facing housing instability. The program is especially helpful for individuals seeking emergency rental assistance in Las Vegas, Nevada, where housing costs are high. HopeLink offers rental assistance, utility help, and housing counseling services.Eviction Prevention CHAP ProgramThe Eviction Prevention CHAP (Coronavirus Housing Assistance Program) provides both rental and housing assistance. These options are available to the individuals and families impacted by the recent pandemic. The program prevents evictions by offering financial support to cover overdue (and current) rent. These services help keep struggling families in their homes while they work to overcome hardships.Section 8 NevadaSection 8 is a federal program that's administered by Nevada's Public Housing Authorities (PHAs). The program provides low-income individuals and families with rental assistance. This way, they can secure and maintain affordable housing. Through Section 8, residents receive housing vouchers that cover a portion of their rental costs. Their income covers the rest of the housing expenses in question.Rental and Deposit Assistance ProgramThe Rental and Deposit Assistance Program provides Nevada residents with financial aid to cover rental costs and move-in expenses. These may include the first month's rent, security deposits, and ongoing rental assistance. This program is designed to support Nevadans who are transitioning into stable housing but may be short on the funds they need to cover beginning home expenses.Who Qualifies for Emergency Rental Assistance?Each program has its own set of requirements, but generally, applicants need to meet one or more of the following criteria.Limited Income: Household income must usually be at or below 80% of the area's median income (AMI). In some cases, priority is given to households with incomes below 50% of the AMI.Financial Hardship: Families who have fallen into financial hardship (such as job loss, health conditions, or reduced hours) will likely qualify.Housing Instability: Applicants who are either homeless or at risk of becoming homeless will likely qualify for assistance.How to Pursue Nevada Emergency Rental AssistanceDespite the fact that several Nevada emergency rental assistance programs exist, finding the right one can be difficult. Fortunately, there are several additional resources Nevadans can pursue for guidance.&nbsp;If you’re struggling to access Nevada housing programs, contact your local Division of Welfare and Supportive Services center, or visit Nevada 211 for more information. Caseworkers and volunteers for these services can direct you toward resources that meet your family’s needs.&nbsp;The economic impacts on Nevada residents have made it clear that a well-rounded support system is a must. If your family is struggling, research each program's resources, requirements, and application process so that you can secure housing assistance as quickly as possible.If you need more information about Nevada’s housing assistance options, check out the Affordable Housing Hub’s Section 8 resources, or explore open waiting lists.

### New Hampshire Emergency Rental Assistance: 2025 Application Guide
The COVID-19 pandemic caused an increase in housing instability that is still impacting people today. Here are some New Hampshire emergency rental assistance programs that might be able to help you.New Hampshire Emergency Rental Assistance ProgramThe New Hampshire Emergency Rental Assistance Program (NHERAP) offers financial help to New Hampshire residents who can’t make their rental or utility payments due to the COVID-19 crisis. The New Hampshire Housing Finance Authority (NHHFA) runs this program in conjunction with the Governor’s Office for Emergency Relief Recovery (GOFERR). Qualified households can receive funds for past due and future rent payments, utility bills, and housing expenses.&nbsp;To qualify for this program, you need to:Earn 80% or less of the local median household income.Be facing housing instability.Demonstrate financial hardship, significant financial obligation, or loss of income due to the COVID-19 pandemic.HomeHelpNHThe HomeHelpNH program offers both rental and mortgage assistance to residents of New Hampshire who are facing housing insecurity through eviction or foreclosure. Qualifying households receive financial support and counseling through local housing agencies to maintain stable housing. Depending on your situation, they may also be able to help you with free civil legal services for eviction cases.To qualify, you’ll need to:&nbsp;Be a resident of New Hampshire.Experience facing eviction or foreclosure.Have documented proof of financial hardship.New Hampshire Housing Finance Authority Housing Choice Voucher ProgramNew Hampshire Housing Finance Authority (NHHFA) Housing Choice Voucher Program gives low-income New Hampshire residents access to safe and affordable housing. Qualifying households pay a portion of their rent and utilities determined by their gross adjusted income. The remainder of their rent is paid by the New Hampshire Housing Authority.&nbsp;Recipients of NHHFA housing vouchers choose their own housing, which must meet criteria ensuring the health and safety of residents. To qualify for this program, you must:Earn 50% of the local median household income or less.Be a New Hampshire resident.Have proof that you are a U.S. citizen or eligible immigrant.Veterans Affairs Supportive Housing ProgramThe Veterans Affairs Supportive Housing Program (HUD-VASH) serves qualifying homeless veterans with funding, clinical services, and case management. CAP agencies offer residents workforce services, HeadStart, fuel assistance, and more programs to further reduce the financial strain families face.&nbsp;Local groups offer programs that cater to the unique needs of their communities and may have different eligibility criteria than other state or federal programs. Funds can be used for past-due rent, future rent, general housing costs, and utility payments. Local CAP agencies process applications for this program.&nbsp;To qualify for this program, you’ll need to:Earn 80% or less of the local median household income.&nbsp;Be facing housing insecurity or homelessness.Have at least one member of the household who has qualified for unemployment, experienced loss of wages, or suffered significant financial hardship due to the COVID-19 pandemic.How Emergency Rental Programs Help New Hampshire CommunitiesSince the onset of the COVID-19 pandemic, homelessness and housing insecurity have become more frequent struggles for residents of New Hampshire and the nation. Emergency rental programs provide relief to renters struggling to pay their bills and keep them in the communities where they’ve built connections. Funds cover short-term rental assistance to eligible households. The program focuses on mediation between landlords and tenants and providing housing stability for senior citizens and individuals with disabilities.&nbsp;&nbsp;To be eligible for this program, your household:Must earn 80% or less of the local median household income.Cannot currently receive rental assistance from another program.Needs to have documentation of financial loss due to COVID-19.City of Albuquerque Emergency Rental AssistanceThe City of Albuquerque offers eligible residents up to 15 months of assistance with back rent, current rent, and future rent payments. Bernalillo County also administers a separate emergency rental assistance program for residents outside of the Albuquerque city limits.To qualify for emergency rental assistance in Albuquerque, New Mexico, your household must::Earn 80% or less of the local median household income.Demonstrate the threat of homelessness.Show documentation of financial loss due to COVID-19.Reside in Albuquerque.CARES Rental and Utility Assistance: Bernalillo CountyEligible residents of Bernalillo County can receive up to $5,000 in emergency rental assistance through CARES funding. To date, more than 2,898 residents have been able to pay off back rent and avoid evictions through this program.&nbsp;To qualify for this program:Rental payments must be past due because of the COVID-19 pandemic.The household must earn 80% or less of the local median household income.Households must demonstrate the threat of homelessness.Recipients must reside in Bernalillo County.HHH Health &amp; Social Service Centers Emergency Rental &amp; Utility Assistance ProgramThis program is a great option for people who need NM emergency rental assistance quickly. Funds are limited and services are provided on a first-come, first-served basis, so interested residents should apply promptly. Contact your local Health &amp; Social Services Center for eligibility information or to start an application.&nbsp;To qualify for this program, your household must::Earn 80% or less of the local median household income.Demonstrate the threat of homelessness.Show documentation of financial loss due to COVID-19.Doña Ana County Eviction Prevention and Diversion ProgramResidents of Doña Ana County who are facing eviction can apply for help with back rent and utility bills. Applicants can check the status of their case online at any time during the process, which makes it easier to stay on top of any updates.&nbsp;To qualify, residents must:Earn 50% or less of the local median household income.Have documentation of imminent eviction.Show that they experienced financial loss due to COVID-19.Reside in Doña Ana County.Emergency Rental and Mortgage Assistance Program (ERMAP): Santa Fe CountySanta Fe County offers eligible residents emergency grants through ERMAP to cope with the impact of the COVID-19 crisis. Residents can use funds from this program to pay past-due rent and utility bills.&nbsp;To qualify for this program, you must:Reside in Santa Fe County.Have experienced loss of work on or after March 1, 2020.Currently be behind on rent.Earn 80% or less of the local median household income.The Importance and Impact of Rental Assistance in New MexicoThe COVID-19 pandemic has forced many residents of New Mexico out of their homes due to loss of work and wages. Losing friends and neighbors harms any community and weakens important social ties. Programs that keep people in their homes support community connections and breathe new life into areas affected by the pandemic.Getting Help With Rent in New MexicoTaking control of housing instability can feel overwhelming but there are programs to help. If you need help paying rent or utilities, these programs can help you figure out how to close the gap, keep you in your home, and help you get back on your feet. Many program administrators offer help applying for programs in person and over the phone. To learn more about emergency rental assistance programs in your area, try out the Affordable Housing Hub’s search tool.

### New York Emergency Rental Assistance: 2025 Application Guide
If you’re experiencing housing instability in New York State, there are options available to you. New York has several affordable housing programs and emergency rental assistance initiatives that can provide immediate aid to those in need.New York’s emergency rental assistance programs are designed to offer short-term financial assistance to individuals and families struggling to find or keep housing. The amount and type of emergency rental assistance for which you could be eligible varies depending on factors like the city in which you live and the specific program through which you are seeking aid. Most programs prioritize the elderly, people with disabilities, needy families with children, and anyone facing dire, immediate crises.Is the New York Emergency Rental Assistance Program (ERAP) Still Accepting Applications?As of 2023, New York State is no longer accepting new applications for the Emergency Rental Assistance Program (ERAP). This program previously offered relief to low and moderate-income households at risk of homelessness.&nbsp;Although New York is no longer accepting new ERAP applications, your application might still be in progress. If you submitted an application before the deadline and are still waiting to hear back, you should contact the New York State Office of Temporary and Disability Assistance (OTDA) using the contact information listed for your county. You can also find information about where to go for emergency rental assistance in Rochester, NY, and other areas of New York State that are ineligible for ERAP benefits.Where Can I Get Emergency Rental Assistance in New York in 2025?If you did not submit an ERAP application before the deadline and you need emergency rental assistance now, you can find resources through your local department of social services. New York’s Department of Social Services (DSS) includes the Department of Homeless Services (DHS) and the Human Resources Administration (HRA), which collectively work to connect individuals with relevant rental assistance programs.New York State Rental Assistance ProgramsIf you are in need of emergency rental assistance in New York, there are several programs that may be available to you.Family Homelessness &amp; Eviction Prevention Supplement (FHEPS)The Family Homelessness &amp; Eviction Prevention Supplement (FHEPS) is intended for families with children who receive cash assistance under the Temporary Aid to Needy Families program (TANF) and are facing eviction or have been evicted. It also supports families who have lost their housing due to domestic violence or health and safety issues.&nbsp;To be eligible for FHEPS, your household must be receiving cash assistance and include at least one child under 18, a child who is 18 years old and attending school full-time, or a pregnant individual. FHEPS may also be able to supplement your rent to help you secure and maintain stable housing.CityFHEPSCityFHEPS is another program administered by New York’s Department of Social Services. It consolidates the previous LINC, SEPS, and CITYFEPS rental assistance initiatives into a single, streamlined emergency rental assistance program. The new program is designed to make rent payments more manageable so that individuals and families can achieve and maintain housing stability.To qualify for CityFHEPS, your household must have an income at or below 200% of the federal poverty level, as well as meet certain additional criteria, such as facing eviction in court or including a member at risk of homelessness who has served in the U.S. Armed Forces.&nbsp;Special One-Time Assistance (SOTA)New York’s Special One-Time Assistance (SOTA) program offers a unique solution for eligible Department of Homeless Services clients that pays one year of rent for single adults or households that have spent significant time living in a shelter, helping them to move into more stable housing.&nbsp;SOTA is available to families with children who have spent at least 90 days in a shelter, or to single adults or adult families who have spent at least 90 of the past 365 days in a shelter. The rent must not exceed 40% of the household’s total current or projected income.&nbsp;To be eligible, the DSS must determine that your household is likely to be able to continue to pay its rent with recurring income from employment or other, long-term benefits after the SOTA benefits have ended.More Information About Emergency Rental Assistance Programs in NY StateIf you live in New York State and you are facing eviction or need immediate rental assistance, it's important to act quickly. Have all necessary documentation ready when contacting a rental assistance agency. You should also make sure you know your rights as a tenant in New York State. New York tenants facing eviction in Housing Court may be eligible for free legal services.If you have more questions about emergency rental assistance, our other rental assistance resources might have the answers you’re looking for.

### North Carolina Emergency Rental Assistance: 2024 Application Guide
Emergency rental assistance programs are designed to aid families and individuals who are unable to pay their rent due to unforeseen circumstances — especially those who are potentially facing eviction or another immediate crisis.&nbsp;In North Carolina, emergency rental assistance programs provide temporary relief from homelessness while also empowering people to become self-sufficient. North Carolina offers a range of emergency rental assistance programs designed to help people in need of immediate, short-term housing aid.&nbsp;Emergency Rental Assistance Programs in NCIf you’re seeking emergency rental assistance in North Carolina, you have numerous options depending on your specific needs and situation.&nbsp;Some cities have their own programs in place for supporting residents in need of temporary rental assistance. For example, if you’re looking for emergency rental assistance in Greensboro, NC, you may be able to receive aid directly through the Greensboro Housing &amp; Neighborhood Development Department.If your local city government does not offer an emergency rental assistance program of its own, you still have several other options at the state level.Work First Family Assistance (WFFA)Work First Family Assistance (WFFA) is North Carolina’s implementation of the federal Temporary Assistance for Needy Families (TANF) program. It offers various forms of support to families who are struggling to help them achieve economic independence, including short-term training, employment services, financial counseling, and many other resources aimed at increasing job readiness and retention.To be eligible for assistance through the Work First program, your household must meet certain requirements.To apply for assistance from the Work First program in North Carolina, contact your local Department of Social Services directly. You can also apply online via the ePASS website. Before applying for Work First assistance, you must also register for the First Stop Employment Assistance Program with the Employment Security Commission.Work First Emergency AssistanceWork First Emergency Assistance is designed to provide immediate, short-term help to families in the Work First program with urgent needs such as utility shut-offs or eviction notices. Emergency assistance offered through North Carolina’s Work First program is intended to address specific, non-recurring episodes of need; it’s not meant to serve as ongoing financial support.To qualify for Work First Emergency Assistance, your household must include a child living with a relative and its total income must not exceed 200% of the federal poverty level (in addition to meeting the criteria for Work First program eligibility).NC Emergency Solutions GrantThe NC Emergency Solutions Grant (ESG) program is one of North Carolina’s best resources for individuals and families who are experiencing homelessness or at risk of becoming homeless. Grant funds are administered to communities in North Carolina through local governments and non-profit organizations, which use ESG funding to support a wide variety of social and emergency housing solutions throughout the state.Emergency shelters offer essential services like case management and health services to shelter residents.Street outreach connects unsheltered homeless individuals with emergency shelters and other necessary services.Prevention initiatives provide financial services such as rental assistance and utility payments to prevent homelessness.Rapid re-housing helps homeless individuals and families facing eviction secure permanent housing quickly and provides support to help them maintain housing stability.Reach out to your local Coordinated Entry contact for more information about how to get connected with ESG-funded services in your community.North Carolina Housing Finance Agency (NCHFA)The North Carolina Housing Finance Agency (NCHFA) offers emergency rental assistance through the Housing Choice Voucher Program. This program offers rental subsidies to low-income families to help them afford safe and sanitary housing in the private market. To apply, contact your local Public Housing Authority.The NCHFA also collaborates with the Supportive Housing Development Program to fund housing projects for special needs populations, including the homeless and disabled.U.S. Department of Housing and Urban Development (HUD)The Department of Housing and Urban Development (HUD) supports several programs that aim to increase the availability of affordable housing. Low-income renters in North Carolina may be able to secure reduced rent through the Department of Housing and Urban Development’s subsidized apartments program. You can search for apartments near you that are eligible for HUD rental subsidization on the HUD website.Get Help Finding Emergency Rental Assistance Programs in North CarolinaIf you’re not sure where to begin searching for emergency rental assistance in North Carolina, United Way of North Carolina is a great place to start. Dial 2-1-1 for help finding housing assistance or other social services in your area.You might also find the information you’re looking for in one of our other emergency rental assistance resources.
